\title{Relational Analysis for Quantum Key Distribution}
\author{Junlin}
\date{Oct 2025}

\begin{document}

\maketitle

\section{Formal System Soundness}

\subsection{Program Model}
\subsubsection{Syntax}

\begin{definition}[Variable Names to Address Indexes]
  \[
  \overset{\textbf{Quantum variables}}{\overbrace{
  \bar q \mapsto [1,\ldots,n_q]
  }}
  \qquad
  \overset{\textbf{Probability registers}}{\overbrace{
  p \mapsto [1,\ldots,n_p]
  }}
  \qquad
  \overset{\textbf{Classical registers}}{\overbrace{
  x \mapsto [1,\ldots,n_x]
  }} .
  \]
  
  Addresses are defined as
  \[
  (\mathsf{Quantum}\quad \mathsf{Int})
  \mid
  (\mathsf{Probability}\quad \mathsf{Int})
  \mid
  (\mathsf{Classical}\quad \mathsf{Int}) .
  \]
  \end{definition}


\begin{definition}[Logical Lists, Length, and Descriptor Views]
Logical list names are written
  \[
  g,h,g_0,g_1,\ldots .
  \]
  Each logical list name has a fixed register sort
  \[
  \mathsf{Quantum},
  \qquad
  \mathsf{Probability},
  \qquad
  \text{or}
  \qquad
  \mathsf{Classical}.
  \]
  The base variable such as
  \[
  \bar q,
  \qquad
  p,
  \qquad
  x
  \]
  is also a logical list name of the corresponding sort.
  
  A descriptor store \(\xi\) assigns to each logical list name \(g\) a descriptor
  view
  \[
  \operatorname{desc}_{\xi}(g)=(\ell_g,\alpha_g),
  \]
  where
  \[
  \ell_g\in\mathbb N,
  \qquad
  \alpha_g:\{1,\ldots,\ell_g\}\to \mathsf{addresses}.
  \]
  
  A descriptor command may overwrite the descriptor stored under a logical list
  name. Such an overwrite changes only how future logical references are
  resolved. The physical register memories are fixed address-indexed memories. Descriptor
  commands do not create, delete, copy, or move physical addresses.
  
  An item in logical list \(g[i]\) is well formed at \(\xi\) only when
  \[
  \operatorname{desc}_{\xi}(g)=(\ell_g,\alpha_g)
  \qquad
  \text{and}
  \qquad
  1\le i\le \ell_g.
  \]
  It resolves to
  \[\alpha_g(i).
  \]
  
  For lists, they resolve to
  \[(\alpha_g(1),\ldots,\alpha_g(n)),
  \qquad
  n\le \ell_g.
  \]
  
  In our system, we separate descriptor data from register data:
  \[
  \text{descriptor data: filters, descriptor integers, and descriptor views,}
  \]
  \[
  \text{register data: payload at physical addresses.}
  \]
  \end{definition}


  \begin{definition}[Static Logical Indices]
    In the following core language, every displayed index
    \[
    i,j,t
    \]
    in a logical reference such as
    \[
    g[i],
    \qquad
    x[i],
    \qquad
    \bar q[j]
    \]
    is a fixed positive natural number at the syntax level. It is not a runtime
    integer expression and not a descriptor integer.
    
    Expression-indexed selected-qubit notation such as
    \[
    \bar q[e_1,\ldots,e_k]\asteq U(e)
    \]
    is syntax sugar only. It expands into finite case analysis over fixed
    natural-number references before denotation.
    \end{definition}



    \begin{definition}[Syntax]
      Statements are divided by command mode.
      
      Descriptor commands update descriptor data:
      \[
      C_D ::=
      f :=_{\$}\mathbf{shuffle}(m)_N
      \mid
      \iota := \mathbf{length}(g)
      \]
      \[
      \mid
      (g_0,g_1)
      :=
      \mathbf{select}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\ \mathbf{for}\ g
      \mid
      g
      :=
      \mathbf{merge}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\ \mathbf{for}\ g_0,g_1 .
      \]
      
      Descriptor integer expressions are
      \[
      J ::= N \mid \iota .
      \]
      
      Register commands read or update register payloads after resolving logical
      references:
      \begin{align*}
      C_R ::=~&
      \mathbf{skip}
      \mid
      \mathbf{abort}
      \mid
      x[i] := E
      \mid
      p :=_{\$}\mathbf{rand}(n)
      \mid
      p :=_{\$} \textit{rand}_{n}(C_m)
      \\
      &\mid
      \bar q[i] := \ket{0}
      \mid
      \bar q[i] \asteq U
      \mid
      x[i] := \mathcal{M}[\bar q[j]]
      \mid
      C_{R,0};C_{R,1}
      \\
      &\mid
      \mathbf{if}\ B \rightarrow C_{R,0},\ \mathbf{else}\rightarrow C_{R,1} .
      \end{align*}
       
      Programs are generated by
      \[
      S ::=
      C_D
      \mid C_R
      \mid S_0;S_1 .
      \]
      
      A command
      \[
      f:=_{\$}\mathbf{shuffle}(m)_N
      \]
      samples a filter of length \(N\) with exactly \(m\) one-bits.
      
      A command
      \[
      \iota:=\mathbf{length}(g)
      \]
      stores the current descriptor length of \(g\).
      
      The commands
      \[
      (g_0,g_1)
      :=
      \mathbf{select}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\ \mathbf{for}\ g
      \]
      and
      \[
      g
      :=
      \mathbf{merge}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\ \mathbf{for}\ g_0,g_1
      \]
      update descriptor views only.
\end{definition}


\begin{definition}[Classical Expressions and Predicates]
Classical value types
\[
\tau ::= \mathsf{Bit}\mid \mathsf{Int}.
\]

for
\[
E ::=
a
\mid \iota
\mid x[i].
\]

\[
B ::=
\top
\mid \bot
\mid E_1=E_2
\mid E_1<E_2
\mid E_1\leq E_2
\mid \neg B
\mid B_1\land B_2
\mid B_1\lor B_2 .
\]

We use \(E_1\neq E_2,\quad E_1>E_2,\quad E_1\geq E_2\)
as standard abbreviations. Predicates \(B\) are guards.
\end{definition}


\subsubsection{\textbf{Semantics}}

\begin{definition}[Descriptor Stores and Register States]
  A descriptor store \(\xi\) maps filter names to finite bitstrings, descriptor
  integer names to integers, and logical list names to descriptor views.

For \(F\in\{0,1\}^N\), its Hamming weight is
\[
\operatorname{wt}(F)
\stackrel{\triangle}{=}
|\{t:1\le t\le N,\ F_t=1\}|.
\]
  
  
  For filter descriptors, write
  \[
  \mathsf{BitList}(N)
  =
  \{0,1\}^{N},
  \qquad
  \mathsf{Filt}(m,N)
  =
  \{F\in\{0,1\}^{N}:\operatorname{wt}(F)=m\}.
  \]


  All code linear algebra is over \(\mathbb F_2\).  A code matrix descriptor \(C_m\) determines a fixed non-empty binary linear code
\[
\mathsf{Code}_n(C_m)\subseteq \mathbb F_2^n,
\]

If \(C_m\) is used as a generator matrix, then
\[
\mathsf{Code}_n(C_m)=\operatorname{rowspan}(C_m).
\]
If \(C_m\) is used as a parity-check matrix, then
\[
\mathsf{Code}_n(C_m)
=
\ker(C_m)
=
\{c\in\mathbb F_2^n:C_m c^{\mathsf T}=0\}.
\]

  Let
  \[
  \mathcal H_{\mathsf D}
  =
  \operatorname{span}\{\ket{\xi}:\xi\text{ is a descriptor store}\}
  \]
  be the classical descriptor space, and let
  \[
  \mathcal H_{\mathsf R}
  \]
  be the physical register memory.

For any Hilbert space \(\mathcal H\), define

\[
\operatorname{Pos}_{\le1}(\mathcal H)
\stackrel{\triangle}{=}
\{A\in\mathcal L(\mathcal H):A\succeq0,\ \operatorname{Tr}(A)\le1\}.
\]
  
  A descriptor-register c-q state is a positive sub-normalized operator
  \[
  \Delta
  \in
  \operatorname{Pos}_{\le 1}
  \left(
  \mathcal H_{\mathsf D}\otimes\mathcal H_{\mathsf R}
  \right)
  \]
  that is classical on the descriptor component:
  \[
  \Delta
  =
  \sum_{\xi}
  \ket{\xi}\bra{\xi}_{\mathsf D}
  \otimes
  \rho_{\xi}.
  \]
  The state itself is the single c-q state \(\Delta\); the displayed sum is its
  semantic block decomposition.
  
  The trace condition is
  \[
  \operatorname{Tr}(\Delta)\le 1.
  \]
  Trace-\(1\) states are admissible initial states. Program denotations may
  produce sub-normalized states.

  Well-typed states are classical on all classical and probability registers:
\[
\rho_{\xi}
=
\sum_c
\ket c\bra c_{\mathsf{Cl/Prob}}
\otimes
\rho_{\xi,c}^{\mathsf Q}.
\]
  
  For descriptor-block notation, write
  \[
  \Delta[\xi]\stackrel{\triangle}{=}\rho_{\xi}.
  \]
  \end{definition}



    \begin{definition}[Resolution and Filter-Indexed Views]
      The notation \(\mathsf{phys}_{\xi}(u)\) is an address-resolution abbreviation induced by descriptor views. It returns physical addresses. For a logical reference,
      \[
      \mathsf{phys}_{\xi}(g[i])
      =
      \alpha_g(i),
      \qquad
      \text{where }
      \operatorname{desc}_{\xi}(g)=(\ell_g,\alpha_g).
      \]
      
      For lists,
      \[
      \mathsf{phys}_{\xi}(g[1,\ldots,n])
      =
      (\alpha_g(1),\ldots,\alpha_g(n)).
      \]

      For whole lists,
\[
\mathsf{phys}_{\xi}(g)
=
(\alpha_g(1),\ldots,\alpha_g(\ell_g)),
\qquad
\operatorname{desc}_{\xi}(g)=(\ell_g,\alpha_g).
\]
      
      If \(\xi(f)=F\), define
      \[
      g^{f}
      \stackrel{\triangle}{=}
      (g|_{F=0},g|_{F=1}),
      \]
      with relative order preserved inside \(g|_{F=0}\) or \(g|_{F=1}\). Thus, when
      \[
      \operatorname{desc}_{\xi}(g)=(\ell_g,\alpha_g),
      \]
      \[
      \mathsf{phys}_{\xi}(g^{f})
      =
      ((\alpha_g(t):1\le t\le \ell_g,\ F_t=0)
      ,(\alpha_g(t):1\le t\le \ell_g,\ F_t=1)).
      \]
      
      For views \(g_0,g_1\), define
      \[
      (g_0,g_1)^{\uparrow f}
      \]
      by
      \[
      \mathsf{phys}_{\xi}((g_0,g_1)^{\uparrow f})
      =
      \text{the unique interleaving of }
      \mathsf{phys}_{\xi}(g_0),
      \mathsf{phys}_{\xi}(g_1)
      \text{ according to }\xi(f).
      \]
      
      The notations \(u^{f}\) and \((u_0,u_1)^{\uparrow f}\) extend componentwise to
parenthesized packages of views. They are defined only when

\[
F\in\{0,1\}^{\ell_g}.
\]

      Resolution of paired views is componentwise:
      \[
      \mathsf{phys}_{\xi,\xi'}(u,u')
      =
      \left(
      \mathsf{phys}_{\xi}(u),
      \mathsf{phys}_{\xi'}(u')
      \right).
      \]
      \end{definition}

      \begin{definition}[Static Admissibility]
        Program denotations are defined only for statically admissible programs. We
        write
        \[
        \Gamma\vdash_{\mathsf{wf}} S
        \]
        for this judgment.
        

Descriptor-dependent admissibility is checked by descriptor-flow typing, never
by register-payload assertions.
        
        If
        \[
        \Gamma\not\vdash_{\mathsf{wf}} S,
        \]
        then
        \[
        \sem S
        \]
        is undefined. This is static rejection, not execution of
        \[
        \mathbf{abort}.
        \]
        \end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Static Rejection Conditions]
For a descriptor store \(\xi\), write
\[
\xi\models_{\mathsf{wf}}S
\]
when the following command-specific conditions hold.

For
\[
f:=_{\$}\mathbf{shuffle}(m)_N,
\]
\[
\xi\models_{\mathsf{wf}}f:=_{\$}\mathbf{shuffle}(m)_N
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
0\le m\le N.
\]

For
\[
\iota:=\mathbf{length}(g),
\]
\[
\xi\models_{\mathsf{wf}}\iota:=\mathbf{length}(g)
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\operatorname{desc}_{\xi}(g)\ \text{is defined}.
\]

For
\[
(g_0,g_1):=
\mathbf{select}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\ \mathbf{for}\ g,
\]
with
\[
\operatorname{desc}_{\xi}(g)=(\ell_g,\alpha_g),
\qquad
e=\llbracket J\rrbracket_{\xi},
\]
\[
\xi\models_{\mathsf{wf}}
(g_0,g_1):=
\mathbf{select}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\ \mathbf{for}\ g
\]
iff
\[
\xi(f)\in\{0,1\}^{N},
\qquad
e=\ell_g\le N,
\qquad
\operatorname{sort}(g_0)=\operatorname{sort}(g_1)=\operatorname{sort}(g).
\]

For
\[
g:=
\mathbf{merge}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\ \mathbf{for}\ g_0,g_1,
\]
with
\[
\operatorname{desc}_{\xi}(g_0)=(\ell_{g_0},\alpha_{g_0}),
\qquad
\operatorname{desc}_{\xi}(g_1)=(\ell_{g_1},\alpha_{g_1}),
\qquad
e=\llbracket J\rrbracket_{\xi},
\]
\[
\xi\models_{\mathsf{wf}}
g:=
\mathbf{merge}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\ \mathbf{for}\ g_0,g_1
\]
iff
\[
\xi(f)\in\{0,1\}^{N},
\qquad
e=N,
\]
\[
|\{t:1\le t\le N,\ \xi(f)_t=0\}|=\ell_{g_0},
\qquad
|\{t:1\le t\le N,\ \xi(f)_t=1\}|=\ell_{g_1},\qquad\ell_{g_0}+\ell_{g_1}=N
\]
\[
\operatorname{sort}(g)=\operatorname{sort}(g_0)=\operatorname{sort}(g_1).
\]

For sequencing,
\[
\xi\models_{\mathsf{wf}}S_0;S_1
\]
iff
\[
\xi\models_{\mathsf{wf}}S_0
\]
and every descriptor store produced from \(\xi\) by the descriptor effect of
\(S_0\) satisfies \(S_1\)'s static conditions.

Finally,
\[
\Gamma\vdash_{\mathsf{wf}}S
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
\forall \xi\models\Gamma.\;\xi\models_{\mathsf{wf}}S.
\]
If this fails, \(S\) is statically rejected and \(\sem S\) is undefined.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Operational Semantics]
In this definition, the transition relation is used only for programs satisfying
the static admissibility judgment
\[
\Gamma\vdash_{\mathsf{wf}} S.
\]
Ill-formed programs have no transition.

A configuration is a pair
\[
C=\langle S,\Delta\rangle,
\]
where \(S\) is a program or the termination symbol \(\downarrow\), and
\(\Delta\) is a descriptor-register c-q state. The operational semantics is the
transition relation
\[
\longrightarrow
\]
defined by the transition rules in Figure~\ref{fig:operational-semantics}.
\end{definition}


\begin{figure}[H]
\centering
\scriptsize

\[
\begin{array}{ll}
\text{\rm (Shuffle)}
&
\displaystyle
\left\langle
f:=_{\$}\mathbf{shuffle}(m)_N,\Delta
\right\rangle
\longrightarrow
\left\langle
\downarrow,
\sum_{\xi}
\sum_{F\in\mathsf{Filt}(m,N)}
\frac{1}{|\mathsf{Filt}(m,N)|}
\ket{\xi[f\mapsto F]}\bra{\xi[f\mapsto F]}_{\mathsf D}
\otimes
\Delta[\xi]
\right\rangle
\\[4ex]

\text{\rm (Length)}
&
\displaystyle
\left\langle
\iota:=\mathbf{length}(g),\Delta
\right\rangle
\longrightarrow
\left\langle
\downarrow,
\sum_{\xi}
\ket{\xi[\iota\mapsto \ell_g]}\bra{\xi[\iota\mapsto \ell_g]}_{\mathsf D}
\otimes
\Delta[\xi]
\right\rangle
\end{array}
\]

\noindent
\begin{minipage}[t]{0.48\textwidth}
\[
\begin{aligned}
&
\text{\rm (Select)}
\quad
\left\langle C_D,\Delta\right\rangle
\longrightarrow
\left\langle
\downarrow,
\sum_{\xi}
\ket{\xi_{\mathsf{sel}}}\bra{\xi_{\mathsf{sel}}}_{\mathsf D}
\otimes
\Delta[\xi]
\right\rangle .
\end{aligned}
\]
\end{minipage}
\hfill
\begin{minipage}[t]{0.48\textwidth}
\[
\begin{aligned}
&
\text{\rm (Merge)}
\quad
\left\langle C_D,\Delta\right\rangle
\longrightarrow
\left\langle
\downarrow,
\sum_{\xi}
\ket{\xi_{\mathsf{mrg}}}\bra{\xi_{\mathsf{mrg}}}_{\mathsf D}
\otimes
\Delta[\xi]
\right\rangle .
\end{aligned}
\]
\end{minipage}

\vspace{0.5ex}

\noindent
\begin{minipage}[t]{0.35\textwidth}
\[
\begin{array}{ll}
\text{\rm (Skip)}
&
\langle \mathbf{skip},\Delta\rangle
\longrightarrow
\langle \downarrow,\Delta\rangle
\\[1.2ex]

\text{\rm (Abort)}
&
\langle \mathbf{abort},\Delta\rangle
\longrightarrow
\langle \downarrow,0\rangle
\end{array}
\]
\end{minipage}
\hfill
\begin{minipage}[t]{0.60\textwidth}
\[
\begin{array}{ll}
\text{\rm (Seq-1)}
&
\displaystyle
\frac{
\langle S_0,\Delta\rangle
\longrightarrow
\langle S'_0,\Delta'\rangle
\qquad
S'_0\neq\downarrow
}{
\langle S_0;S_1,\Delta\rangle
\longrightarrow
\langle S'_0;S_1,\Delta'\rangle
}
\\[3ex]

\text{\rm (Seq-2)}
&
\displaystyle
\frac{
\langle S_0,\Delta\rangle
\longrightarrow
\langle \downarrow,\Delta'\rangle
}{
\langle S_0;S_1,\Delta\rangle
\longrightarrow
\langle S_1,\Delta'\rangle
}
\end{array}
\]
\end{minipage}

\[
\begin{array}{ll}
\text{\rm (Rand)}
&
\displaystyle
\left\langle
p:=_{\$}\mathbf{rand}(n),\Delta
\right\rangle
\longrightarrow
\left\langle
\downarrow,
\sum_{\xi}
\ket{\xi}\bra{\xi}_{\mathsf D}
\otimes
\left(
2^{-n}
\sum_{s\in\{0,1\}^{n}}
\ket{s}_{\vec a}\bra{s}
\otimes
\operatorname{Tr}_{\vec a}(\Delta[\xi])
\right)
\right\rangle
\\[4ex]

\text{\rm (Assign)}
&
\displaystyle
\left\langle
x[i]:=E,\Delta
\right\rangle
\longrightarrow
\left\langle
\downarrow,
\sum_{\xi}
\ket{\xi}\bra{\xi}_{\mathsf D}
\otimes
\left(
\sum_v
\ket v_{a_x}\bra v
\otimes
\operatorname{Tr}_{a_x}
\left(
\Pi_{E=v,\xi}\Delta[\xi]\Pi_{E=v,\xi}
\right)
\right)
\right\rangle .
\end{array}
\]

\noindent
\begin{minipage}[t]{0.48\textwidth}
\[
\begin{aligned}
&
\text{\rm (Init)}
\quad
\left\langle
\bar q[i]:=\ket0,\Delta
\right\rangle
\longrightarrow
\left\langle
\downarrow,
\sum_{\xi}
\ket{\xi}\bra{\xi}_{\mathsf D}
\otimes
\left(
\ket0_{a_q}\bra0
\otimes
\operatorname{Tr}_{a_q}(\Delta[\xi])
\right)
\right\rangle
\end{aligned}
\]
\end{minipage}
\hfill
\begin{minipage}[t]{0.48\textwidth}
\[
\begin{aligned}
&
\text{\rm (UT)}
\quad
\left\langle
\bar q[i]\asteq U,\Delta
\right\rangle
\longrightarrow
\left\langle
\downarrow,
\sum_{\xi}
\ket{\xi}\bra{\xi}_{\mathsf D}
\otimes
\left(
U_{a_q}\Delta[\xi]U_{a_q}^{\dagger}
\right)
\right\rangle .
\end{aligned}
\]
\end{minipage}

\vspace{0.5ex}

\[
\begin{array}{ll}
\text{\rm (Meas)}
&
\displaystyle
\left\langle
x[i]:=\mathcal M[\bar q[j]],\Delta
\right\rangle
\longrightarrow
\left\langle
\downarrow,
\sum_{\xi}
\ket{\xi}\bra{\xi}_{\mathsf D}
\otimes
\left(
\sum_{r\in[m]}
\ket r_{a_x}\bra r
\otimes
M^{a_q}_r
\operatorname{Tr}_{a_x}(\Delta[\xi])
M^{a_q\dagger}_r
\right)
\right\rangle .
\end{array}
\]

\[
\begin{array}{ll}
\text{\rm (CodeRand)}
&
\displaystyle
\left\langle
p:=_{\$}\textit{rand}_{n}(C_m),\Delta
\right\rangle
\longrightarrow
\left\langle
\downarrow,
\sum_{\xi}
\ket{\xi}\bra{\xi}_{\mathsf D}
\otimes
\left(
\frac{1}{|\mathsf{Code}_n(C_m)|}
\sum_{c\in\mathsf{Code}_n(C_m)}
\ket c_{\vec a}\bra c
\otimes
\operatorname{Tr}_{\vec a}(\Delta[\xi])
\right)
\right\rangle .
\end{array}
\]

\[
\begin{aligned}
&
\text{\rm (If)}
\left\langle
\mathbf{if}\ B\rightarrow C_{R,0},\ \mathbf{else}\rightarrow C_{R,1},
\Delta
\right\rangle
\longrightarrow
\left\langle
\downarrow,
\sum_{\xi}
\ket{\xi}\bra{\xi}_{\mathsf D}
\otimes
\left[
\mathcal E^{C_{R,0}}_{\xi}
\left(
\Pi_{B,\xi}\Delta[\xi]\Pi_{B,\xi}
\right)
+
\mathcal E^{C_{R,1}}_{\xi}
\left(
\Pi_{\neg B,\xi}\Delta[\xi]\Pi_{\neg B,\xi}
\right)
\right]
\right\rangle .
\end{aligned}
\]

\caption{Transition rules.}
\Description{Transition rules.}
\label{fig:operational-semantics}
\end{figure}

Descriptor integer expressions are evaluated by
\[
\llbracket N\rrbracket_{\xi}=N,
\qquad
\llbracket \iota\rrbracket_{\xi}=\xi(\iota).
\]

In rule \({\rm (Length)}\), the descriptor of \(g\) in branch \(\xi\) is
\[
\operatorname{desc}_{\xi}(g)=(\ell_g,\alpha_g).
\]

In rule \({\rm (Select)}\),
\[
C_D=
(g_0,g_1):=
\mathbf{select}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\ \mathbf{for}\ g,
\qquad
e=\llbracket J\rrbracket_{\xi},
\qquad
\xi(f)=F,
\qquad
\operatorname{desc}_{\xi}(g)=(\ell_g,\alpha_g).
\]
We write \(F[s]\) for the \(s\)-th bit of the filter list \(F\).
The store \(\xi_{\mathsf{sel}}\) is the descriptor store obtained from \(\xi\)
after this select operation: it changes only the descriptors of \(g_0\) and
\(g_1\). It sets
\[
\operatorname{desc}_{\xi_{\mathsf{sel}}}(g_0)
=
\left(
|\{1\le s\le e:F[s]=0\}|,
\ t\mapsto (\alpha_g(s):1\le s\le e,\ F[s]=0)[t]
\right),
\]
and
\[
\operatorname{desc}_{\xi_{\mathsf{sel}}}(g_1)
=
\left(
|\{1\le s\le e:F[s]=1\}|,
\ t\mapsto (\alpha_g(s):1\le s\le e,\ F[s]=1)[t]
\right).
\]
All other descriptor bindings are unchanged.



In rule \({\rm (Merge)}\),
\[
C_D=
g:=
\mathbf{merge}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\ \mathbf{for}\ g_0,g_1,
\qquad
e=\llbracket J\rrbracket_{\xi},
\qquad
\xi(f)=F,
\]
and
\[
\operatorname{desc}_{\xi}(g_0)=(\ell_{g_0},\alpha_{g_0}),
\qquad
\operatorname{desc}_{\xi}(g_1)=(\ell_{g_1},\alpha_{g_1}).
\]
The store \(\xi_{\mathsf{mrg}}\) is the descriptor store obtained from \(\xi\)
after this merge operation: it changes only the descriptor of \(g\). It sets
\[
\operatorname{desc}_{\xi_{\mathsf{mrg}}}(g)
=
(e,\alpha_h),
\]
where
\[
\alpha_h(t)=
\begin{cases}
\alpha_{g_0}\!\left(|\{1\le s\le t:F[s]=0\}|\right),
&
F[t]=0,
\\[0.6ex]
\alpha_{g_1}\!\left(|\{1\le s\le t:F[s]=1\}|\right),
&
F[t]=1.
\end{cases}
\]
All other descriptor bindings are unchanged.

In rule \({\rm (Rand)}\),
\[
p:=_{\$}\mathbf{rand}(n),
\qquad
\vec a=\mathsf{phys}_{\xi}(p[1,\ldots,n]).
\]

In rule \({\rm (Assign)}\),
\[
x[i]:=E,
\qquad
a_x=\mathsf{phys}_{\xi}(x[i]).
\]
For a classical expression \(E\), \(\Pi_{E=v,\xi}\) is the branchwise
classical projector where \(E\) evaluates to \(v\) under \(\xi\).

In rule \({\rm (Init)}\),
\[
\bar q[i]:=\ket0,
\qquad
a_q=\mathsf{phys}_{\xi}(\bar q[i]).
\]

In rule \({\rm (UT)}\),
\[
\bar q[i]\asteq U,
\qquad
a_q=\mathsf{phys}_{\xi}(\bar q[i]).
\]

In rule \({\rm (Meas)}\),
\[
x[i]:=\mathcal M[\bar q[j]],
\qquad
\mathcal M=\{M_r\}_{r\in[m]},
\]
and
\[
a_x=\mathsf{phys}_{\xi}(x[i]),
\qquad
a_q=\mathsf{phys}_{\xi}(\bar q[j]).
\]

In rule \({\rm (CodeRand)}\),
\[
p:=_{\$}\textit{rand}_{n}(C_m),
\qquad
\vec a=\mathsf{phys}_{\xi}(p[1,\ldots,n]).
\]

For conditionals, \(\Pi_{B,\xi}\) is the branchwise classical projector
defined by the predicate \(B\), with descriptor integers interpreted using
\(\xi\).

In rule \({\rm (If)}\), the branch effects \(\mathcal E^{C_{R,0}}_{\xi}\) and
\(\mathcal E^{C_{R,1}}_{\xi}\) are the corresponding register effects given by
the register-command clauses.

\begin{definition}[Denotational Semantics]
For any statically admissible program \(S\), its denotation is the map
\[
\sem S
\]
defined by
\[
\sem S(\Delta)
=
\sum
\left\{
\left|
\Delta'
:
\langle S,\Delta\rangle
\longrightarrow^{*}
\langle \downarrow,\Delta'\rangle
\right|
\right\},
\]
where \(\longrightarrow^{*}\) is the reflexive and transitive closure of
\(\longrightarrow\), and \(\{|\cdot|\}\) denotes a multiset.
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Approximate Classical-Quantum Lifting]
      For descriptor-register c-q states
      \[
      \Delta
      \qquad
      \text{and}
      \qquad
      \Delta',
      \]
      write
      \[
      \Delta\ \Phi^\delta\ \Delta'
      \]
      if there exists a descriptor-register c-q witness
      \[
      \pi
      =
      \sum_{\xi,\xi'}
      \ket{\xi}\bra{\xi}_{\mathsf D_L}
      \otimes
      \ket{\xi'}\bra{\xi'}_{\mathsf D_R}
      \otimes
      \omega_{\xi,\xi'}
      \]
      such that
      \[
      \omega_{\xi,\xi'}
      \in
      \operatorname{SepD}_{\le 1}(\mathcal H^L_{\mathsf R}:\mathcal H^R_{\mathsf R}),
      \]
      \[
      \operatorname{Tr}_{\mathsf D_R,\mathsf R_R}(\pi)
      =
      \Delta,
      \qquad
      \operatorname{Tr}_{\mathsf D_L,\mathsf R_L}(\pi)
      =
      \Delta',
      \]
      and, with assertion
      \[\llbracket\Phi\rrbracket
      \stackrel{\triangle}{=}
      \sum_{\xi,\xi'}
      \ket{\xi}\bra{\xi}_{\mathsf D_L}
      \otimes
      \ket{\xi'}\bra{\xi'}_{\mathsf D_R}
      \otimes
      \llbracket\Phi\rrbracket^R_{\xi,\xi'},
      \]
      \[
      \operatorname{Tr}
      \left(
      \llbracket\Phi\rrbracket
      \pi
      \right)
      \ge
      \operatorname{Tr}(\pi)-\delta.
      \]
    here,
    \[
      \operatorname{SepD}_{\le 1}(\mathcal H_L:\mathcal H_R)
      \]
      denotes the set of sub-normalized separable positive operators:
      \[
      \omega
      =
      \sum_k p_k\,
      \rho^L_k\otimes\rho^R_k,
      \qquad
      p_k\ge 0,
      \qquad
      \sum_k p_k\le 1,
      \]
      where
      \[
      \rho^L_k\in D(\mathcal H_L),
      \qquad
      \rho^R_k\in D(\mathcal H_R).
      \]

      
      For \(\delta=0\), write
      \[
      \Delta\ \Phi\ \Delta' .
      \]
      \end{definition}


\begin{definition}[Logical Assertions and Raw Resolution]
Single-side view expressions are generated by
\[
u ::=
g[i]
\mid
g[1,\ldots,n]
\mid
g
\mid
g^{f}
\mid
(g_0,g_1)^{\uparrow f}
\mid
(u_1,\ldots,u_k).
\]
Packages resolve componentwise:
\[
\mathsf{phys}_{\xi}((u_1,\ldots,u_k))
=
\mathsf{phys}_{\xi}(u_1)\cdots\mathsf{phys}_{\xi}(u_k).
\]
Equality on packages follows the same sort-sensitive convention.

Paired view indices are generated by
\[
\mathcal V ::=
(u,u')
\mid
[(u_1,u'_1),\ldots,(u_k,u'_k)].
\]

Descriptor formulas are generated by
\[
\chi ::=
\top
\mid
\bot
\mid
\equiv_{(f,f')}
\mid
\equiv_{(\iota,\iota')}
\mid
\Pi_f^N
\mid
\Pi_f^{m,N}
\mid
\chi_0\land\chi_1
\mid
\chi_0\lor\chi_1
\mid
\neg\chi .
\]

Register assertions over logical views are generated by
\[
R_{\mathcal V} ::=
A_{\mathcal V}
\mid
\equiv_{(u,u')}
\mid
\equiv_{\mathcal V}
\mid
\Pi_z^\mu
\mid
\Pi_z^\Omega
\mid
\Pi_p^{C_m,n}
\mid
\equiv_{(z,z')}^\mu
\mid
\equiv_{(z,z')}^\Omega .
\]
For paired view indices,
\[
\equiv_{\mathcal V}
\]
is pointwise equality over all pairs in \(\mathcal V\).

Logical assertions are generated by
\[
\Phi ::=
\chi
\mid
R_{\mathcal V}
\mid
\Phi_0\land\Phi_1
\mid
\Phi_0\lor\Phi_1
\mid
\neg\Phi
\mid
\Phi * C_{\mathcal U}
\mid
\operatorname{proj}\!\left(
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal U}(\Phi)
\right).
\]
When the displayed register views of an assertion are collected in
\(\mathcal V\), we may write it as \(\Phi_{\mathcal V}\).

Raw assertions are generated by
\[
\widetilde{\Phi} ::=
\widetilde{\top}
\mid
\widetilde{\bot}
\mid
\widetilde R
\mid
\widetilde{\Phi}_0\land\widetilde{\Phi}_1
\mid
\widetilde{\Phi}_0\lor\widetilde{\Phi}_1
\mid
\neg\widetilde{\Phi}
\mid
\widetilde{\Phi} * \widetilde C_{\widetilde{\mathcal U}}
\mid
\operatorname{proj}\!\left(
\operatorname{Tr}_{\widetilde{\mathcal U}}(\widetilde{\Phi})
\right),
\]
where
\[
\widetilde R ::=
\widetilde A_{\widetilde{\mathcal V}}
\mid
\widetilde{\equiv}_{(\vec a,\vec a')}
\mid
\widetilde{\equiv}_{\widetilde{\mathcal V}}
\mid
\widetilde{\Pi}_{\vec a}^{\mu}
\mid
\widetilde{\Pi}_{\vec a}^{\Omega}
\mid
\widetilde{\Pi}_{\vec a}^{C_m,n}
\mid
\widetilde{\equiv}_{(\vec a,\vec a')}^{\mu}
\mid
\widetilde{\equiv}_{(\vec a,\vec a')}^{\Omega}.
\]
A raw assertion contains only physical register addresses and no descriptor
data.

The first interpretation map resolves logical assertions to raw assertions:
\[
\llbracket \Phi\rrbracket_{\xi,\xi'}=\widetilde{\Phi}.
\]
Descriptor formulas resolve to raw truth values:
\[
\llbracket \top\rrbracket_{\xi,\xi'}=\widetilde{\top},
\qquad
\llbracket \bot\rrbracket_{\xi,\xi'}=\widetilde{\bot},
\]
\[
\llbracket \equiv_{(f,f')}\rrbracket_{\xi,\xi'}
=
\begin{cases}
\widetilde{\top}, & \xi(f)=\xi'(f'),\\
\widetilde{\bot}, & \text{otherwise},
\end{cases}
\]
\[
\llbracket \equiv_{(\iota,\iota')}\rrbracket_{\xi,\xi'}
=
\begin{cases}
\widetilde{\top}, & \xi(\iota)=\xi'(\iota'),\\
\widetilde{\bot}, & \text{otherwise},
\end{cases}
\]
\[
\llbracket \Pi_f^N\rrbracket_{\xi,\xi'}
=
\begin{cases}
\widetilde{\top}, & \xi(f)\in\{0,1\}^N,\\
\widetilde{\bot}, & \text{otherwise},
\end{cases}
\]
\[
\llbracket \Pi_f^{m,N}\rrbracket_{\xi,\xi'}
=
\begin{cases}
\widetilde{\top}, & \xi(f)\in\mathsf{Filt}(m,N),\\
\widetilde{\bot}, & \text{otherwise}.
\end{cases}
\]

Logical register assertions resolve by replacing logical views with physical
views. If a displayed view is not well formed under \((\xi,\xi')\), the result
is \(\widetilde{\bot}\). In particular,
\[
\llbracket A_{\mathcal V}\rrbracket_{\xi,\xi'}
=
\widetilde A_{\mathsf{phys}_{\xi,\xi'}(\mathcal V)}.
\]

For finite-support \(\mu\) and finite domain \(\Omega\),
\[
\llbracket \Pi_z^\mu\rrbracket_{\xi,\xi'}
=
\widetilde{\Pi}_{\mathsf{phys}_{\xi}(z)}^\mu,
\qquad
\llbracket \Pi_z^\Omega\rrbracket_{\xi,\xi'}
=
\widetilde{\Pi}_{\mathsf{phys}_{\xi}(z)}^\Omega,
\]
\[
\llbracket \Pi_p^{C_m,n}\rrbracket_{\xi,\xi'}
=
\widetilde{\Pi}_{\mathsf{phys}_{\xi}(p[1,\ldots,n])}^{C_m,n}.
\]
For paired classical or probability views,
\[
\llbracket \equiv_{(z,z')}^\mu\rrbracket_{\xi,\xi'}
=
\widetilde{\equiv}_{(\mathsf{phys}_{\xi}(z),\mathsf{phys}_{\xi'}(z'))}^{\mu},
\]
\[
\llbracket \equiv_{(z,z')}^\Omega\rrbracket_{\xi,\xi'}
=
\widetilde{\equiv}_{(\mathsf{phys}_{\xi}(z),\mathsf{phys}_{\xi'}(z'))}^{\Omega}.
\]

List and package equality is sort-sensitive. Classical and probability lists
use pointwise equality. Quantum lists use block equality on the resolved ordered
blocks. Thus
\[
\llbracket \equiv_{(u,u')}\rrbracket_{\xi,\xi'}
=
\widetilde{\equiv}_{(\mathsf{phys}_{\xi}(u),\mathsf{phys}_{\xi'}(u'))},
\]
with the sort-sensitive interpretation fixed by the resolved views. For paired
view indices,
\[
\llbracket\equiv_{\mathcal V}\rrbracket_{\xi,\xi'}
\]
is the conjunction of the resolved component equalities.

For filter-indexed equality,
\[
\llbracket \equiv_{(g^f,g'^{f'})}\rrbracket_{\xi,\xi'}
\]
is the sort-sensitive equality on the resolved ordered views when
\[
\xi(f)=\xi'(f'),
\]
and both filters have the common whole-list length. Otherwise it is
\(\widetilde{\bot}\).

The first interpretation map commutes with logical connectives:
\[
\llbracket \Phi_0\land\Phi_1\rrbracket_{\xi,\xi'}
=
\llbracket\Phi_0\rrbracket_{\xi,\xi'}
\land
\llbracket\Phi_1\rrbracket_{\xi,\xi'},
\]
\[
\llbracket \Phi_0\lor\Phi_1\rrbracket_{\xi,\xi'}
=
\llbracket\Phi_0\rrbracket_{\xi,\xi'}
\lor
\llbracket\Phi_1\rrbracket_{\xi,\xi'},
\qquad
\llbracket\neg\Phi\rrbracket_{\xi,\xi'}
=
\neg\llbracket\Phi\rrbracket_{\xi,\xi'}.
\]
It also resolves trace and frame views:
\[
\llbracket
\operatorname{proj}\!\left(
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal U}(\Phi)
\right)
\rrbracket_{\xi,\xi'}
=
\operatorname{proj}\!\left(
\operatorname{Tr}_{\mathsf{phys}_{\xi,\xi'}(\mathcal U)}
(\llbracket\Phi\rrbracket_{\xi,\xi'})
\right),
\]
\[
\llbracket \Phi*C_{\mathcal U}\rrbracket_{\xi,\xi'}
=
\llbracket\Phi\rrbracket_{\xi,\xi'}
*
\llbracket C_{\mathcal U}\rrbracket_{\xi,\xi'}.
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Raw Register Assertions and Projector Semantics]
Raw assertions denote projectors on the physical left/right register memory:
\[
\llbracket \widetilde{\Phi}\rrbracket^R
\in
\operatorname{Proj}
\left(
\mathcal H^L_{\mathsf R}\otimes\mathcal H^R_{\mathsf R}
\right).
\]

Raw truth values are interpreted by
\[
\llbracket\widetilde{\top}\rrbracket^R
=
I_{\mathcal H^L_{\mathsf R}\otimes\mathcal H^R_{\mathsf R}},
\qquad
\llbracket\widetilde{\bot}\rrbracket^R
=
0_{\mathcal H^L_{\mathsf R}\otimes\mathcal H^R_{\mathsf R}}.
\]

Atomic raw assertions are interpreted by
\[
\llbracket \widetilde A_{\widetilde{\mathcal V}}\rrbracket^R
=
A_{\widetilde{\mathcal V}}.
\]

For finite-support \(\mu\) and finite domain \(\Omega\),
\[
\llbracket \widetilde{\Pi}_{\vec a}^{\mu}\rrbracket^R
=
\sum_{a\in\operatorname{supp}(\mu)}
\ket a_{\vec a}\bra a,
\qquad
\llbracket \widetilde{\Pi}_{\vec a}^{\Omega}\rrbracket^R
=
\sum_{a\in\Omega}
\ket a_{\vec a}\bra a.
\]
For code-randomized probability views,
\[
\llbracket \widetilde{\Pi}_{\vec a}^{C_m,n}\rrbracket^R
=
\sum_{c\in\mathsf{Code}_n(C_m)}
\ket c_{\vec a}\bra c .
\]

For classical or probability equality,
\[
\llbracket
\widetilde{\equiv}_{(\vec a,\vec a')}^{\Omega}
\rrbracket^R
=
\sum_{a\in\Omega}
\ket a_{\vec a}\bra a
\otimes
\ket a_{\vec a'}\bra a,
\]
and
\[
\llbracket
\widetilde{\equiv}_{(\vec a,\vec a')}^{\mu}
\rrbracket^R
=
\sum_{a\in\operatorname{supp}(\mu)}
\ket a_{\vec a}\bra a
\otimes
\ket a_{\vec a'}\bra a.
\]

For quantum equality on ordered blocks,
\[
\llbracket
\widetilde{\equiv}^{\mathsf q}_{(\vec q,\vec q')}
\rrbracket^R
=
\frac12
\left(
I+\mathsf{SWAP}_{\vec q,\vec q'}
\right).
\]
For unlabelled raw equality
\[
\widetilde{\equiv}_{(\vec a,\vec a')},
\]
the sort of the physical addresses determines whether the classical,
probability, or quantum clause is used.  Equality on raw paired view indices is
the conjunction of the component equalities.

For raw projective assertions, define
\[
\llbracket \widetilde{\Phi}\land\widetilde{\Psi}\rrbracket^R
=
\operatorname{proj}
\left(
\operatorname{Im}\llbracket \widetilde{\Phi}\rrbracket^R
\cap
\operatorname{Im}\llbracket \widetilde{\Psi}\rrbracket^R
\right),
\]
\[
\llbracket \widetilde{\Phi}\lor\widetilde{\Psi}\rrbracket^R
=
\operatorname{proj}
\left(
\operatorname{Im}\llbracket \widetilde{\Phi}\rrbracket^R
+
\operatorname{Im}\llbracket \widetilde{\Psi}\rrbracket^R
\right),
\]
\[
\llbracket \neg\widetilde{\Phi}\rrbracket^R
=
I_{\mathcal H^L_{\mathsf R}\otimes\mathcal H^R_{\mathsf R}}
-
\llbracket \widetilde{\Phi}\rrbracket^R .
\]
If
\[
\llbracket\widetilde{\Phi}\rrbracket^R
\llbracket\widetilde{\Psi}\rrbracket^R
=
0,
\]
then
\[
\widetilde{\Phi}\lor\widetilde{\Psi}
=
\widetilde{\Phi}+\widetilde{\Psi}.
\]

For raw trace assertions,
\[
\llbracket
\operatorname{proj}\!\left(
\operatorname{Tr}_{\widetilde{\mathcal U}}(\widetilde{\Phi})
\right)
\rrbracket^R
=
\operatorname{proj}
\left(
\operatorname{Tr}_{\widetilde{\mathcal U}}
\left(
\llbracket\widetilde{\Phi}\rrbracket^R
\right)
\right).
\]

The separated conjunction
\[
\widetilde{\Phi} * \widetilde C_{\widetilde{\mathcal U}}
\]
is well formed only when the auxiliary resource contexts certify the required
liveness and separation. Semantically,
\[
\llbracket
\widetilde{\Phi} * \widetilde C_{\widetilde{\mathcal U}}
\rrbracket^R
=
\llbracket\widetilde{\Phi}\land
\widetilde C_{\widetilde{\mathcal U}}\rrbracket^R .
\]

The projector interpretation of a logical assertion is
\[
\llbracket \Phi\rrbracket^R_{\xi,\xi'}
\stackrel{\triangle}{=}
\llbracket
\llbracket \Phi\rrbracket_{\xi,\xi'}
\rrbracket^R .
\]

Write \(\equiv\) when the view index is clear.
\end{definition}

    
\subsection{\textbf{Relational Judgment System}}
\begin{definition}[Symbolic Proof Context]
\(\Gamma\) contains persistent symbolic facts: protocol parameters, arithmetic,
and name assumptions. Liveness/freshness/separation are
certified by a resource system, not stored in \(\Gamma\). Entailments have form
\[
\Gamma\vDash \Phi\Longrightarrow\Psi.
\]
This means that, for all descriptor-store pairs satisfying \(\Gamma\),
\[
\llbracket\Phi\rrbracket^R_{\xi,\xi'}
\le
\llbracket\Psi\rrbracket^R_{\xi,\xi'} .
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Classical-Quantum Relational Judgment]
    A relational judgment has the form
    \[
    \Gamma
    \vdash
    P\sim_{\delta}P'
    :
    \Phi_{\mathcal V}
    \Longrightarrow
    \Psi_{\mathcal W}.
    \]
    
    The judgment is well formed only when
    \[
    \Gamma\vdash_{\mathsf{wf}} P
    \qquad
    \text{and}
    \qquad
    \Gamma\vdash_{\mathsf{wf}} P'.
    \]
    
    It is valid iff for all well-typed \(\Delta,\Delta'\), every witness \(\pi\)
    for
    \[
    \Delta\ \Phi_{\mathcal V}\ \Delta'
    \]
    with
    \[
    \operatorname{supp}_{\mathsf{cl}}(\pi)\models\Gamma
    \]
    satisfies
    \[
    \llbracket P\rrbracket(\Delta)
    \ \Psi_{\mathcal W}^{\delta}\
    \llbracket P'\rrbracket(\Delta').
    \]
    
    For \(\delta=0\), write
    \[
    \Gamma
    \vdash
    P\sim P'
    :
    \Phi_{\mathcal V}
    \Longrightarrow
    \Psi_{\mathcal W}.
    \]
    \end{definition}


    \begin{definition}[Auxiliary-Certified Relational Derivation]
      \[
      \Gamma\vdash A\#B
      \]
      means that \(\Gamma\)'s symbolic facts hold and the auxiliary resource system
      certifies that the resources or descriptor dependencies in \(A\) and \(B\) do
      not interfere.
      
      For register views, \(\#\) certifies the needed left/right liveness and
      physical separation. For descriptor dependency sets, \(\#\) certifies
      descriptor-name disjointness.

      For mixed footprints, \(\#\) checks both descriptor-name disjointness and
resolved register-resource separation.
      \end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Command-Mode Footprints]
For every program \(P\), we use four footprint components:
\[
\operatorname{dacc}(P),
\qquad
\operatorname{dupd}(P),
\]
\[
\operatorname{racc}(P),
\qquad
\operatorname{rupd}(P).
\]

\(\operatorname{dacc},\operatorname{dupd}\) are descriptor-data footprints, and
\(\operatorname{racc},\operatorname{rupd}\) are register-payload footprints.

\[
\operatorname{acc}(P)
\stackrel{\triangle}{=}
\operatorname{dacc}(P)
\cup
\operatorname{racc}(P),
\]
\[
\operatorname{upd}(P)
\stackrel{\triangle}{=}
\operatorname{dupd}(P)
\cup
\operatorname{rupd}(P).
\]

For paired programs,
\[
\operatorname{acc}(P,P')
\stackrel{\triangle}{=}
\operatorname{acc}(P)\cup\operatorname{acc}(P'),
\qquad
\operatorname{upd}(P,P')
\stackrel{\triangle}{=}
\operatorname{upd}(P)\cup\operatorname{upd}(P').
\]

Updates are included in the corresponding access mode:
\[
\operatorname{dupd}(P)\subseteq \operatorname{dacc}(P),
\qquad
\operatorname{rupd}(P)\subseteq \operatorname{racc}(P).
\]

For descriptor integer expressions,
\[
\operatorname{dacc}(N)=\emptyset,
\qquad
\operatorname{dacc}(\iota)=\{\iota\}.
\]


For classical expressions,
\[
\operatorname{dacc}(a)=\emptyset,
\qquad
\operatorname{racc}(a)=\emptyset,
\]
\[
\operatorname{dacc}(\iota)=\{\iota\},
\qquad
\operatorname{racc}(\iota)=\emptyset,
\]
\[
\operatorname{dacc}(x[i])=\{x\},
\qquad
\operatorname{racc}(x[i])=\{x[i]\},
\]
and
\[
\operatorname{dacc}(E_1+E_2)
=
\operatorname{dacc}(E_1)\cup\operatorname{dacc}(E_2),
\]
\[
\operatorname{racc}(E_1+E_2)
=
\operatorname{racc}(E_1)\cup\operatorname{racc}(E_2).
\]

For predicates \(B\), descriptor and register access footprints are defined
recursively from their subexpressions. The constants \(\top,\bot\) have empty
footprints.

For
\[
f:=_{\$}\mathbf{shuffle}(m)_N,
\]
\[
\operatorname{dacc}=\operatorname{dupd}=\{f\},
\qquad
\operatorname{racc}=\operatorname{rupd}=\emptyset.
\]

For
\[
\iota:=\mathbf{length}(g),
\]
\[
\operatorname{dacc}=\{g,\iota\},
\qquad
\operatorname{dupd}=\{\iota\},
\qquad
\operatorname{racc}=\operatorname{rupd}=\emptyset.
\]

For
\[
(g_0,g_1)
:=
\mathbf{select}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\ \mathbf{for}\ g,
\]
\[
\operatorname{dacc}
=
\{f,g,g_0,g_1\}
\cup
\operatorname{dacc}(J),
\qquad
\operatorname{dupd}=\{g_0,g_1\},
\qquad
\operatorname{racc}=\operatorname{rupd}=\emptyset.
\]

For
\[
g
:=
\mathbf{merge}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\ \mathbf{for}\ g_0,g_1,
\]
\[
\operatorname{dacc}
=
\{f,g,g_0,g_1\}
\cup
\operatorname{dacc}(J),
\qquad
\operatorname{dupd}=\{g\},
\qquad
\operatorname{racc}=\operatorname{rupd}=\emptyset.
\]

For register commands,
\[
\operatorname{dupd}(R)=\emptyset.
\]

For
\[
\mathbf{skip}
\qquad\text{and}\qquad
\mathbf{abort},
\]
all four footprints are empty.

For
\[
x[i]:=E,
\]
\[
\operatorname{dacc}
=
\{x\}\cup\operatorname{dacc}(E),
\]
\[
\operatorname{racc}
=
\{x[i]\}\cup\operatorname{racc}(E),
\qquad
\operatorname{rupd}=\{x[i]\}.
\]

For
\[
p:=_{\$}\mathbf{rand}(n),
\]
\[
\operatorname{dacc}
=
\{p\},
\]
\[
\operatorname{racc}
=
\operatorname{rupd}
=
\{p[1,\ldots,n]\}.
\]

For
\[
p:=_{\$}\textit{rand}_{n}(C_m),
\]
\[
\operatorname{dacc}=\{p\},
\qquad
\operatorname{racc}
=
\operatorname{rupd}
=
\{p[1,\ldots,n]\}.
\]

For
\[
\bar q[i]:=\ket 0,
\]
\[
\operatorname{dacc}=\{\bar q\},
\qquad
\operatorname{racc}=\operatorname{rupd}=\{\bar q[i]\}.
\]

For
\[
\bar q[i]\asteq U,
\]
\[
\operatorname{dacc}=\{\bar q\},
\qquad
\operatorname{racc}=\operatorname{rupd}=\{\bar q[i]\}.
\]

For
\[
x[i]:=\mathcal M[\bar q[j]],
\]
\[
\operatorname{dacc}=\{x,\bar q\},
\]
\[
\operatorname{racc}=\{x[i],\bar q[j]\},
\qquad
\operatorname{rupd}=\{x[i],\bar q[j]\}.
\]

For sequencing,
\[
\operatorname{dacc}(S_0;S_1)
=
\operatorname{dacc}(S_0)\cup\operatorname{dacc}(S_1),
\]
\[
\operatorname{dupd}(S_0;S_1)
=
\operatorname{dupd}(S_0)\cup\operatorname{dupd}(S_1),
\]
\[
\operatorname{racc}(S_0;S_1)
=
\operatorname{racc}(S_0)\cup\operatorname{racc}(S_1),
\]
\[
\operatorname{rupd}(S_0;S_1)
=
\operatorname{rupd}(S_0)\cup\operatorname{rupd}(S_1).
\]

For conditionals,
\[
\operatorname{dacc}
\left(
\mathbf{if}\ B\rightarrow R_0,\ \mathbf{else}\rightarrow R_1
\right)
=
\operatorname{dacc}(B)
\cup
\operatorname{dacc}(R_0)
\cup
\operatorname{dacc}(R_1),
\]
\[
\operatorname{racc}
\left(
\mathbf{if}\ B\rightarrow R_0,\ \mathbf{else}\rightarrow R_1
\right)
=
\operatorname{racc}(B)
\cup
\operatorname{racc}(R_0)
\cup
\operatorname{racc}(R_1),
\]
\[
\operatorname{dupd}
\left(
\mathbf{if}\ B\rightarrow R_0,\ \mathbf{else}\rightarrow R_1
\right)
=
\emptyset,
\]
\[
\operatorname{rupd}
\left(
\mathbf{if}\ B\rightarrow R_0,\ \mathbf{else}\rightarrow R_1
\right)
=
\operatorname{rupd}(R_0)
\cup
\operatorname{rupd}(R_1).
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Footprint Equality]
  For a mixed footprint set \(A\), the notation
  \[
  \equiv_A
  \]
  means the conjunction of the local equalities generated by the typed elements
  of \(A\).
  
  Filter, descriptor-integer, logical-descriptor, and register-payload entries
  respectively generate
  \[
  \equiv_{(f,f')},
  \qquad
  \equiv_{(\iota,\iota')},
  \qquad
  \equiv_{(g,g')},
  \qquad
  \equiv_{(u,u')}.
  \]
  
  Thus
  \[
  \equiv_{\operatorname{acc}(P)}
  \]
  is the local equality needed to run two copies of \(P\) in lockstep, and
  \[
  \equiv_{\operatorname{upd}(P)}
  \]
  is the corresponding equality on updated views.
  \end{definition}

  \begin{definition}[Descriptor Dependencies]
    For view indices, descriptor dependencies are written
    \[
    \operatorname{ddep}(\mathcal V).
    \]
    For ordinary views,
    \[
    \operatorname{ddep}(g[i])
    =
    \operatorname{ddep}(g[1,\ldots,n])
    =
    \operatorname{ddep}(g)
    =
    \{g\}.
    \]
    For descriptor integer expressions,
    \[
    \operatorname{ddep}(N)=\emptyset,
    \qquad
    \operatorname{ddep}(\iota)=\{\iota\}.
    \]
    For induced views,
    \[
    \operatorname{ddep}(g^{f})
    =
    \{g,f\},
    \qquad
    \operatorname{ddep}((g_0,g_1)^{\uparrow f})
    =
    \{g_0,g_1,f\}.
    \]
    For paired and packaged views, dependencies are collected componentwise.
    
    For descriptor formulas,
    \[
    \operatorname{ddep}(\top)
    =
    \operatorname{ddep}(\bot)
    =
    \emptyset,
    \]
    \[
    \operatorname{ddep}(\equiv_{(f,f')})
    =
    \{f,f'\},
    \qquad
    \operatorname{ddep}(\equiv_{(\iota,\iota')})
    =
    \{\iota,\iota'\},
    \]
    \[
    \operatorname{ddep}(\Pi_f^N)
    =
    \operatorname{ddep}(\Pi_f^{m,N})
    =
    \{f\},
    \]
    with Boolean connectives handled by union.
    
    For register assertions,
    \[
    \operatorname{ddep}(R_{\mathcal V})
    =
    \operatorname{ddep}(\mathcal V).
    \]
    For general assertions,
    \[
    \operatorname{ddep}(\chi)
    =
    \text{as above},
    \qquad
    \operatorname{ddep}(R_{\mathcal V})
    =
    \operatorname{ddep}(\mathcal V),
    \]
    and dependencies of compound assertions are collected componentwise. In
    particular,
    \[
    \operatorname{ddep}
    \left(
    \operatorname{proj}
    \left(
    \operatorname{Tr}_{\mathcal U}(\Phi)
    \right)
    \right)
    =
    \operatorname{ddep}(\Phi)\cup\operatorname{ddep}(\mathcal U).
    \]
    \end{definition}

\textbf{Structural proof rules for QKD:}

\[
\text{\rm (Conseq)}
\quad
\frac{
\Gamma
\vDash
\Phi'_{\mathcal V'}
\Longrightarrow
\Phi_{\mathcal V}
\qquad
\Gamma
\vDash
\Psi_{\mathcal W}
\Longrightarrow
\Psi'_{\mathcal W'}
\qquad
\delta\leq\delta'
\qquad
\Gamma
\vdash
P\sim_{\delta}P':
\Phi_{\mathcal V}
\Longrightarrow
\Psi_{\mathcal W}
}{
\Gamma
\vdash
P\sim_{\delta'}P':
\Phi'_{\mathcal V'}
\Longrightarrow
\Psi'_{\mathcal W'}
}.
\]

\[
\text{\rm (Weaken-\(\Gamma\))}
\quad
\frac{
\Gamma
\vdash
P\sim_{\delta}P':
\Phi\Longrightarrow\Psi
\qquad
\Gamma'\vDash\Gamma
}{
\Gamma'
\vdash
P\sim_{\delta}P':
\Phi\Longrightarrow\Psi
}.
\]

\[
\text{\rm (Seq)}
\quad
\frac{
\Gamma
\vdash
P_0\sim_{\delta}P_1:
\Phi\Longrightarrow\Theta
\qquad
\Gamma
\vdash
P'_0\sim_{\delta'}P'_1:
\Theta\Longrightarrow\Psi
}{
\Gamma
\vdash
P_0;P'_0
\sim_{\delta+\delta'}
P_1;P'_1
:
\Phi\Longrightarrow\Psi
}.
\]

\[
\text{\rm (Skip)}
\quad
\Gamma
\vdash
\mathbf{skip}\sim\mathbf{skip}:
\Phi\Longrightarrow\Phi .
\]

\[
\text{\rm (Abort)}
\quad
\Gamma
\vdash
\mathbf{abort}\sim\mathbf{abort}:
\Phi\Longrightarrow\Psi .
\]

\[
\text{\rm (Ident)}
\quad
{
\Gamma
\vdash
P\sim P:
\equiv_{\operatorname{acc} (P)}
\Longrightarrow
\equiv_{\operatorname{upd} (P)}
}.
\]

\[
\text{\rm (Comp)}
\quad
\frac{
\Gamma
\vdash
P\sim_{\delta_1}P':
\equiv_{\mathcal V}
\Longrightarrow
\equiv_{\mathcal V}
\qquad
\Gamma
\vdash
P'\sim_{\delta_2}P'':
\equiv_{\mathcal V}
\Longrightarrow
\equiv_{\mathcal V}
}{
\Gamma
\vdash
P\sim_{\delta_1+\delta_2}P'':
\equiv_{\mathcal V}
\Longrightarrow
\equiv_{\mathcal V}
}.
\]

An assertion \(C_{\mathcal U}\) is indexed by \(\mathcal U\). In
(Classical-Frame\({}^{*}\)), \(C_{\mathcal U}\) is classical or
descriptor-diagonal.
\[
\text{\rm (Classical-Frame${}^{*}$)}
\quad
\frac{
\Gamma
\vdash
P\sim_{\delta}P':
\Phi_{\mathcal V}
\Longrightarrow
\Psi_{\mathcal W}\qquad
\Gamma\vdash
\mathcal U
\#
\operatorname{upd}(P,P')}{
\Gamma
\vdash
P\sim_{\delta}P':
\Phi_{\mathcal V} * C_{\mathcal U}
\Longrightarrow
\Psi_{\mathcal W} * C_{\mathcal U}
}.
\]

\[
\text{\rm (Quantum-Frame${}^{*}$)}
\quad
\frac{
\begin{array}{c}
\Gamma
\vdash
P\sim_{\delta}P':
\Phi_{\mathcal V}
\Longrightarrow
\Psi_{\mathcal W}
\qquad
\Gamma\vdash
\mathcal U
\#
\operatorname{acc}(P,P')
\end{array}
}{
\Gamma
\vdash
P\sim_{\delta}P':
\Phi_{\mathcal V} * C_{\mathcal U}
\Longrightarrow
\Psi_{\mathcal W} * C_{\mathcal U}
}.
\]


\[
\text{\rm (Swap)}
\quad
\frac{
\Gamma\vdash
\operatorname{acc}(P_0)\#
\operatorname{acc}(P_1)
}{
\Gamma
\vdash
P_0;P_1
\sim
P_1;P_0
:
\equiv_{\mathcal V}
\Longrightarrow
\equiv_{\mathcal V}
}.
\]

In (Swap), \(\mathcal V\) is access-covering:
\[
\Gamma\vDash
\equiv_{\mathcal V}
\Longrightarrow
\equiv_{\operatorname{acc}(P_0)\cup\operatorname{acc}(P_1)}.
\]
The same convention applies to (If-Stru-1) and (If-Stru-2).

\textbf{Construct-specific rules for QKD.}


\[
\text{\rm (Assign-classical)}
\quad
\Gamma
\vdash
x[i]:=a_1
\sim
x'[j]:=a_2
:
\Phi
\Longrightarrow
\ket{a_1}_{x[i]}\bra{a_1}
\land
\ket{a_2}_{x'[j]}\bra{a_2}
\land
\operatorname{proj}
\left(
\operatorname{Tr}_{x[i],x'[j]}(\Phi)
\right).
\]

\[
\text{\rm (Assign-classical-L)}
\quad
\Gamma
\vdash
x[i]:=a
\sim
\mathbf{skip}
:
\Phi
\Longrightarrow
\ket a_{x[i]}\bra a
\land
\operatorname{proj}
\left(
\operatorname{Tr}_{x[i]}(\Phi)
\right).
\]

\[
\text{\rm (Init-Quantum)}
\quad
\Gamma
\vdash
\bar q[i]:=\ket 0
\sim
\bar q'[j]:=\ket 0
:
\Phi
\Longrightarrow
\ket 0_{\bar q[i]}\bra 0
\land
\ket 0_{\bar q'[j]}\bra 0
\land
\operatorname{proj}
\left(
\operatorname{Tr}_{\bar q[i],\bar q'[j]}(\Phi)
\right).
\]

\[
\text{\rm (Init-Quantum-L)}
\quad
\Gamma
\vdash
\bar q[i]:=\ket 0
\sim
\mathbf{skip}
:
\Phi
\Longrightarrow
\ket 0_{\bar q[i]}\bra 0
\land
\operatorname{proj}
\left(
\operatorname{Tr}_{\bar q[i]}(\Phi)
\right).
\]



\[
\text{\rm (Rand)}
\quad
\frac{
\Gamma\vDash n=n'
}{
\Gamma
\vdash
p:=_{\$}\mathbf{rand}(n)
\sim
p':=_{\$}\mathbf{rand}(n')
:
\Phi
\Longrightarrow
\equiv_{(p[1,\ldots,n],p'[1,\ldots,n'])}
\land
\operatorname{proj}
\left(
\operatorname{Tr}_{p[1,\ldots,n],p'[1,\ldots,n']}(\Phi)
\right)
}.
\]

\[
\text{\rm (Rand-L)}
\quad
\Gamma
\vdash
p:=_{\$}\mathbf{rand}(n)
\sim
\mathbf{skip}
:
\Phi
\Longrightarrow
\Pi^{\mathbb B^n}_{p[1,\ldots,n]}
\land
\operatorname{proj}
\left(
\operatorname{Tr}_{p[1,\ldots,n]}(\Phi)
\right).
\]


\[
\text{\rm (Shuffle)}
\quad
\frac{
\Gamma
\vDash
m=m'\land N=N'
\qquad
\Gamma\vdash
\operatorname{ddep}(\Phi)\#\{f,f'\}
}{
\Gamma
\vdash
f:=_{\$}\mathbf{shuffle}(m)_N
\sim
f':=_{\$}\mathbf{shuffle}(m')_{N'}
:
\Phi
\Longrightarrow
\Phi\land
\equiv_{(f,f')}
}.
\]

\[
\text{\rm (Shuffle-L)}
\quad
\frac{
\Gamma\vdash
\operatorname{ddep}(\Phi)\#\{f\}
}{
\Gamma
\vdash
f:=_{\$}\mathbf{shuffle}(m)_N
\sim
\mathbf{skip}
:
\Phi
\Longrightarrow
\Phi\land \Pi_f^{m,N}
}.
\]

\[
\text{\rm (Length)}
\quad
\frac{
\Gamma\vdash
\operatorname{ddep}(\Phi)\#\{\iota,\iota'\}
}{
\Gamma
\vdash
\iota:=\mathbf{length}(g)
\sim
\iota':=\mathbf{length}(g')
:
\Phi\land\equiv_{(g,g')}
\Longrightarrow
\Phi\land\equiv_{(\iota,\iota')}
}.
\]

\[
\text{\rm (CodeRand)}
\quad
\frac{
\Gamma
\vDash
C_m=C_m'\land n=n'
}{
\Gamma
\vdash
p :=_{\$}\textit{rand}_{n}(C_m)
\sim
p':=_{\$}\textit{rand}_{n'}(C_m')
:
\Phi
\Longrightarrow
\equiv_{(p,p')}
\land
\operatorname{proj}
\left(
\operatorname{Tr}_{p,p'}(\Phi)
\right)
}.
\]

\[
\text{\rm (CodeRand-L)}
\quad
\Gamma
\vdash
p :=_{\$}\textit{rand}_{n}(C_m)
\sim
\mathbf{skip}
:
\Phi
\Longrightarrow
\Pi_{p}^{C_m,n}
\land
\operatorname{proj}
\left(
\operatorname{Tr}_{p}(\Phi)
\right).
\]

\[
\text{\rm (IID)}
\quad
\frac{
\Gamma\vDash m=m'\land N=N'
\qquad
\Gamma\vdash
\operatorname{ddep}(\Phi)\#\{f,f'\}
}{
\begin{aligned}
\Gamma
\vdash\;&
f:=_{\$}\mathbf{shuffle}(m)_N;\
p:=_{\$}\mathbf{rand}(N)
\\
&\sim
p':=_{\$}\mathbf{rand}(N');\
f':=_{\$}\mathbf{shuffle}(m')_{N'}:
\\
&
\Phi
\Longrightarrow
\equiv_{(f,f')}
\land
\equiv_{(p^f,p'^{f'})}
\land
\operatorname{proj}
\left(
\operatorname{Tr}_{p[1,\ldots,N],p'[1,\ldots,N']}(\Phi)
\right).
\end{aligned}
}
\]



\[
\text{\rm (UT)}
\quad
\Gamma
\vdash
\bar q[\mathbf i]\asteq U
\sim
\bar q'[\mathbf j]\asteq U'
:
\Phi
\Longrightarrow
\left(
U_{\bar q[\mathbf i]}
\otimes
U'_{\bar q'[\mathbf j]}
\right)
\Phi
\left(
U_{\bar q[\mathbf i]}
\otimes
U'_{\bar q'[\mathbf j]}
\right)^{\dagger}.
\]

\[
\text{\rm (UT-L)}
\quad
\Gamma
\vdash
\bar q[\mathbf i]\asteq U
\sim
\mathbf{skip}
:
\Phi
\Longrightarrow
U_{\bar q[\mathbf i]}
\Phi
U_{\bar q[\mathbf i]}^\dagger .
\]

We write
\[
\Gamma
\vDash
\Phi\Longrightarrow B\leftrightarrow B'
\]
to abbreviate
\[
\Gamma\vDash \Phi\land B\Longrightarrow B',
\qquad
\Gamma\vDash \Phi\land\neg B\Longrightarrow \neg B'.
\]
We write
\[
\Gamma
\vDash
\Phi\Longrightarrow_B\{\Theta_0,\Theta_1\}
\]
to abbreviate
\[
\Gamma\vDash \Phi\land B\Longrightarrow\Theta_0,
\qquad
\Gamma\vDash \Phi\land\neg B\Longrightarrow\Theta_1.
\]

\[
\text{\rm (If)}
\quad
\frac{
\Gamma
\vDash
\Phi\Longrightarrow B\leftrightarrow B'
\qquad
\Gamma
\vDash
\Phi\Longrightarrow_B\{\Theta_0,\Theta_1\}
\qquad
\Gamma
\vdash
R_0\sim R'_0:
\Theta_0\Longrightarrow\Psi
\qquad
\Gamma
\vdash
R_1\sim R'_1:
\Theta_1\Longrightarrow\Psi
}{
\Gamma
\vdash
\mathbf{if}\ B\rightarrow R_0,\ \mathbf{else}\rightarrow R_1
\sim
\mathbf{if}\ B'\rightarrow R'_0,\ \mathbf{else}\rightarrow R'_1
:
\Phi
\Longrightarrow
\Psi
}.
\]

\[
\text{\rm (If-L)}
\quad
\frac{
\Gamma
\vDash
\Phi\Longrightarrow_B\{\Theta_0,\Theta_1\}
\qquad
\Gamma
\vdash
R_0\sim R:
\Theta_0\Longrightarrow\Psi
\qquad
\Gamma
\vdash
R_1\sim R:
\Theta_1\Longrightarrow\Psi
}{
\Gamma
\vdash
\mathbf{if}\ B\rightarrow R_0,\ \mathbf{else}\rightarrow R_1
\sim
R
:
\Phi
\Longrightarrow
\Psi
}.
\]


\begin{definition}[Measurement Condition]
Let
\[
\mathcal M_1=\{M_1^{r}\}_{r\in[m]},
\qquad
\mathcal M_2=\{M_2^{r}\}_{r\in[m]}
\]
be two measurements with the same outcome set
\([m]=\{1,\ldots,m\}\). The measurement condition
\[
\Gamma
\vDash
\mathcal M_1\approx\mathcal M_2:
\Phi_{\mathcal V}
\Longrightarrow
\Psi_{\mathcal W}
\]
means that, for every \(r\in[m]\) and every pair of well-typed
c-q states \(\Delta,\Delta'\), if
\[
\Delta\ \Phi_{\mathcal V}\ \Delta'
\]
has a witness \(\pi\) satisfying
\[
\operatorname{supp}_{\mathsf{cl}}(\pi)\models\Gamma,
\]
then
\[
M_1^r\Delta M_1^{r\dagger}
\ \Psi_{\mathcal W}\
M_2^r\Delta'M_2^{r\dagger}.
\]

For a one-sided measurement, the condition
\[
\Gamma
\vDash
\mathcal M\approx\mathcal I:
\Phi_{\mathcal V}
\Longrightarrow
\Psi_{\mathcal W}
\]
means that, for every pair of well-typed c-q states
\(\Delta,\Delta'\), if
\[
\Delta\ \Phi_{\mathcal V}\ \Delta'
\]
has a witness \(\pi\) satisfying
\[
\operatorname{supp}_{\mathsf{cl}}(\pi)\models\Gamma,
\]
then there exists a family of c-q states
\[
\{\Delta'_r\}_{r\in[m]}
\qquad\text{such that}\qquad
\sum_{r\in[m]}\Delta'_r=\Delta',
\]
and, for every \(r\in[m]\),
\[
M^r\Delta M^{r\dagger}
\ \Psi_{\mathcal W}\
\Delta'_r.
\]
\end{definition}

For a classical logical reference \(z\) with values in \([m]\), define
\[
\Pi_z^{[m]}
\stackrel{\triangle}{=}
\sum_{r\in[m]}
\ket r_z\bra r .
\]
For paired classical logical references \(z,z'\), define
\[
\equiv^{[m]}_{(z,z')}
\stackrel{\triangle}{=}
\sum_{r\in[m]}
\ket r_z\bra r
\otimes
\ket r_{z'}\bra r .
\]

\[
\text{\rm (Meas)}
\quad
\frac{
\Gamma
\vDash
\mathcal M_1\approx\mathcal M_2:
\Phi_{\mathcal V}
\Longrightarrow
\Psi_{\mathcal W}
}{
\Gamma
\vdash
x[i]:=\mathcal M_1[\bar q[j]]
\sim
x'[i']:=\mathcal M_2[\bar q'[j']]
:
\Phi_{\mathcal V}
\Longrightarrow
\equiv^{[m]}_{(x[i],x'[i'])}
\land
\operatorname{proj}
\left(
\operatorname{Tr}_{x[i],x'[i']}(\Psi_{\mathcal W})
\right)
}.
\]

\[
\text{\rm (Meas-L)}
\quad
\frac{
\Gamma
\vDash
\mathcal M\approx\mathcal I:
\Phi_{\mathcal V}
\Longrightarrow
\Psi_{\mathcal W}
}{
\Gamma
\vdash
x[i]:=\mathcal M[\bar q[j]]
\sim
\mathbf{skip}
:
\Phi_{\mathcal V}
\Longrightarrow
\Pi^{[m]}_{x[i]}
\land
\operatorname{proj}
\left(
\operatorname{Tr}_{x[i]}(\Psi_{\mathcal W})
\right)
}.
\]

\[
\text{\rm (CNOT)}
\quad
{\begin{aligned}
\Gamma
&\vdash
\bar q_1,\bar q_2\asteq \mathrm{CNOT};
\ c[t]:=\mathcal M_{\mathrm{com}}[\bar q_1]
\sim
c'[t']:=\mathcal M_{\mathrm{com}}[\bar q'_1];
\ \mathbf{if}\ c'[t']=0\rightarrow\mathbf{skip},
\ \mathbf{else}\rightarrow \bar q'_2\asteq X :\\ 
&
\equiv_{((\bar q_1,\bar q_2),(\bar q'_1,\bar q'_2))}
\Longrightarrow
\equiv_{(c[t],c'[t'])}
\land
\equiv_{((\bar q_1,\bar q_2),(\bar q'_1,\bar q'_2))}
\end{aligned}}
\]

\[
\text{\rm (If-Stru-1)}
\quad
\frac{
\Gamma\vdash
\operatorname{upd}(c_2)
\#
\operatorname{acc}(b)
}{
\Gamma
\vdash
c_2;\
\mathbf{if}\ b=0\rightarrow c_0,\ \mathbf{else}\rightarrow c_1
\sim
\mathbf{if}\ b=0\rightarrow c_2;c_0,\ \mathbf{else}\rightarrow c_2;c_1
:
\equiv_{\mathcal V}
\Longrightarrow
\equiv_{\mathcal V}
}.
\]

\[
\text{\rm (If-Stru-2)}
\quad
\Gamma
\vdash
(\mathbf{if}\ b=0\rightarrow c_0,\ \mathbf{else}\rightarrow c_1);c_2
\sim
\mathbf{if}\ b=0\rightarrow c_0;c_2,\ \mathbf{else}\rightarrow c_1;c_2
:
\equiv_{\mathcal V}
\Longrightarrow
\equiv_{\mathcal V}.
\]

\begin{definition}[Bad Event Assertion]
Let \(bad\) be a bit-valued failure-event view, also written
\[
bad
\stackrel{\triangle}{=}
\ket 1_{bad}\bra 1
\]
for the projector where \(bad=1\), and define
\[
\neg bad
\stackrel{\triangle}{=}
I-bad
=
\ket 0_{bad}\bra 0.
\]
For a left-side bad event write
\[
\neg bad\otimes I
\]
to act on the left and as identity on the right. This proof-side flag is not a
terminal QKD observation component.
\end{definition}

\[
\text{\rm (UTB)}
\quad
\frac{
\Gamma
\vdash
P'_1\sim_{\delta'}P:
\equiv_{\mathcal V}
\Longrightarrow
\equiv_{\mathcal V}\land(\neg bad\otimes I)
\qquad
\Gamma
\vdash
P\sim_{\delta}P':
\equiv_{\mathcal V}
\Longrightarrow
\equiv_{\mathcal V}
}{
\Gamma
\vdash
P'_1\sim_{\delta+\delta'}P':
\equiv_{\mathcal V}
\Longrightarrow
\equiv_{\mathcal V}\land(\neg bad\otimes I)
}.
\]

\begin{definition}[Uniformity in a Basis]
Let
\(\mathcal B=\{\ket{i}\}_{i=1}^{D}\)
be an orthonormal basis. \(\rho\) is uniform in \(\mathcal B\) iff measurement
in \(\mathcal B\) is uniform:
\[
p_i=\operatorname{Tr}\left(\ket{i}\bra{i}\rho\right)
=\langle i|\rho|i\rangle
=\frac{1}{D}\qquad
(1\le i\le D).
\]
\end{definition}

Uniformity is observable, not uniquely projective; here it is used through the
sufficient condition \(\ket{+}^{\otimes\ell}\) before computational-basis
measurement. For
\[
\mathcal B=
\{\ket{s}_{\bar q}:s\in\{0,1\}^{\ell}\},
\]
define
\[
\ket +_{\bar q}
=
\frac{1}{\sqrt{2^\ell}}
\sum_{s\in\{0,1\}^{\ell}}
\ket s_{\bar q},
\qquad
\Phi_{\bar q}^{\mathcal B}
=
\ket +_{\bar q}\bra +.
\]

\[
\text{\rm (Uniform)}
\quad
\frac{
\Gamma
\vDash
\Phi
\Longrightarrow
\Phi_{\bar q}^{\mathcal B}
}{
\Gamma
\vdash
x
:=
\mathcal M_{\mathcal B}[\bar q[1,\ldots,\ell]]
\sim
p'
:=_{\$}
\mathbf{rand}(\ell)
:
\Phi
\Longrightarrow
\equiv_{(x,p')}
}.
\]

% ============================================================
% Descriptor-sensitive sift
% ============================================================
\begin{definition}[Descriptor Alias Notation]
Let \(D_f\) be a descriptor command controlled by the filter \(f\). For a view
set \(\mathcal V\), write
\[
\operatorname{src}_{D_f}(\mathcal V),
\qquad
\operatorname{tgt}_{D_f}(\mathcal V)
\]
for the source-side and target-side versions of \(\mathcal V\).

For
\[
D_f
=
(g_0,g_1)
:=
\mathbf{select}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}~J~\mathbf{for}\ g,
\]
\[
\operatorname{src}_{D_f}(g)=g,
\qquad
\operatorname{tgt}_{D_f}(g)=(g_0,g_1).
\]

If
\[
D_f
=
(\mathcal P_0,\mathcal P_1)
:=
\mathbf{select}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}~J~\mathbf{for}\ \mathcal P,
\]
then
\[
\operatorname{src}_{D_f}(\mathcal P)=\mathcal P,
\qquad
\operatorname{tgt}_{D_f}(\mathcal P)=(\mathcal P_0,\mathcal P_1).
\]

If \(D_f\) selects \(b,\bar q\) into \(b_c,\bar q_c,b_k,\bar q_k\), and a
register command produces \(x_c,x_k\), the rule instance may use
\[
\operatorname{tgt}_{D_f}(b,x)=((b_c,x_c),(b_k,x_k)).
\]

For
\[
D_f
=
g
:=
\mathbf{merge}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}~J~\mathbf{for}\ g_0,g_1,
\]
\[
\operatorname{src}_{D_f}(g)=(g_0,g_1),
\qquad
\operatorname{tgt}_{D_f}(g)=g.
\]

If
\[
D_f
=
\mathcal P
:=
\mathbf{merge}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}~J~\mathbf{for}\ \mathcal P_0,\mathcal P_1,
\]
then
\[
\operatorname{src}_{D_f}(\mathcal P)=(\mathcal P_0,\mathcal P_1),
\qquad
\operatorname{tgt}_{D_f}(\mathcal P)=\mathcal P.
\]
\end{definition}

\begin{definition}[Descriptor Layout Compatibility]
  The check
  \[
  \Gamma
  \vdash
  D_f[\mathcal P]
  \cong
  D'_{f'}[\mathcal P']
  \]
  means that the two descriptor commands have the same descriptor layout form.
  
  For select commands,
  \[
  (\mathcal P_0,\mathcal P_1)
  :=
  \mathbf{select}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\ \mathbf{for}\ \mathcal P
  \cong
  (\mathcal P'_0,\mathcal P'_1)
  :=
  \mathbf{select}_{f'}^{N'}\ \mathbf{from}\ J'\ \mathbf{for}\ \mathcal P'
  \]
  requires that
  \[
  \mathcal P,\mathcal P',
  \qquad
  \mathcal P_0,\mathcal P'_0,
  \qquad
  \mathcal P_1,\mathcal P'_1
  \]
  have the same parenthesized package structure, and that the descriptor formulas
  in the displayed Sift precondition entail
  \[
  N=N',
  \qquad
  J=J',
  \qquad
  \equiv_{(f,f')}.
  \]
  
  For merge commands,
  \[
  \mathcal P
  :=
  \mathbf{merge}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\ \mathbf{for}\ \mathcal P_0,\mathcal P_1
  \cong
  \mathcal P'
  :=
  \mathbf{merge}_{f'}^{N'}\ \mathbf{from}\ J'\ \mathbf{for}\ \mathcal P'_0,\mathcal P'_1
  \]
  requires that
  \[
  \mathcal P,\mathcal P',
  \qquad
  \mathcal P_0,\mathcal P'_0,
  \qquad
  \mathcal P_1,\mathcal P'_1
  \]
  have the same parenthesized package structure, and that the descriptor formulas
  in the displayed Sift precondition entail
  \[
  N=N',
  \qquad
  J=J',
  \qquad
  \equiv_{(f,f')}.
  \]
  
  Select and merge layouts are not compatible with each other.  The check does
  not require equality of list names or equality of register sorts.
  \end{definition}

  \begin{definition}[Register Schema Alignment]
    The check
    \[
    \Gamma
    \vdash
    C_L
    \cong
    C_R
    :
    \mathcal U
    \Rightarrow
    \mathcal W
    \]
    is a Sift-side static check for descriptor-preserving register schemas:
    \[
    \operatorname{dupd}(C_L)
    =
    \operatorname{dupd}(C_R)
    =
    \emptyset .
    \]
    
    The interface
    \[
    \mathcal U\Rightarrow\mathcal W
    \]
    is the complete input/output view interface of the alignment. Its views may be
    ordinary views, filter-indexed views \(u^{f}\), or merge-indexed views
    \(u^{\uparrow f}\).
    
    The check requires that \(C_L\) and \(C_R\), after expanding the displayed
    register sugars, have the same register schema modulo the view pairing specified
    by \(\mathcal U\Rightarrow\mathcal W\). Paired controls, operands, and outputs
    are exactly those displayed in \(\mathcal U\) and \(\mathcal W\). Operation
    parameters are compared under the descriptor formulas in the displayed Sift
    precondition.
    \end{definition}



\[
\text{\rm (Select)}
\quad
\frac{
\Gamma\vDash J=J'
}{
\begin{aligned}
\Gamma
\vdash\;&
(\mathcal P_0,\mathcal P_1)
:=
\mathbf{select}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\ \mathbf{for}\ \mathcal P
\sim
(\mathcal P'_0,\mathcal P'_1)
:=
\mathbf{select}_{f'}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J'\ \mathbf{for}\ \mathcal P'
:
\\
&
\equiv_{(f,f')}\land\equiv_{(\mathcal P,\mathcal P')}
\Longrightarrow
\equiv_{((\mathcal P_0,\mathcal P_1),(\mathcal P'_0,\mathcal P'_1))}
\end{aligned}
}
\]

\[
\text{\rm (Merge)}
\quad
\frac{
\Gamma\vDash J=J'
}{
\begin{aligned}
\Gamma
\vdash\;&
\mathcal P
:=
\mathbf{merge}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\ \mathbf{for}\ \mathcal P_0,\mathcal P_1
\sim
\mathcal P'
:=
\mathbf{merge}_{f'}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J'\ \mathbf{for}\ \mathcal P'_0,\mathcal P'_1
:
\\
&
\equiv_{(f,f')}\land\equiv_{((\mathcal P_0,\mathcal P_1),
          (\mathcal P'_0,\mathcal P'_1))}
\Longrightarrow
\equiv_{(\mathcal P,\mathcal P')}
\end{aligned}
}
\]

\[
\text{\rm (Select-L)}
\quad{
\begin{aligned}
\Gamma
\vdash\;&
(\mathcal P_0,\mathcal P_1)
:=
\mathbf{select}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\ \mathbf{for}\ \mathcal P
\sim
\mathbf{skip}
:
\equiv_{(\mathcal P^f,\mathcal U')}
\Longrightarrow
\equiv_{((\mathcal P_0,\mathcal P_1),\mathcal U')}.
\end{aligned}
}
\]

\[
\text{\rm (Merge-L)}
\quad
{
\begin{aligned}
\Gamma
\vdash\;&
\mathcal P
:=
\mathbf{merge}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\ \mathbf{for}\ \mathcal P_0,\mathcal P_1
\sim
\mathbf{skip}
:
\equiv_{((\mathcal P_0,\mathcal P_1)^{\uparrow f},\mathcal U')}
\Longrightarrow
\equiv_{(\mathcal P,\mathcal U')}.
\end{aligned}
}
\]

\[
\text{\rm (Sift)}
\quad
\frac{
\begin{array}{c}
\Gamma
\vdash
D_f[\mathcal P_{\mathsf{pre}}]
\cong
D'_{f'}[\mathcal P'_{\mathsf{post}}]
\\[0.6ex]
\Gamma
\vdash
C_{\operatorname{tgt}_{D_f}}
\cong
C_{\operatorname{src}_{D'_{f'}}}
:
\mathcal U
\Rightarrow
\mathcal W
\end{array}
}{
\begin{aligned}
\Gamma
\vdash\;&
D_f[\mathcal P_{\mathsf{pre}}];
C_{\operatorname{tgt}_{D_f}}
\sim
C_{\operatorname{src}_{D'_{f'}}};
D'_{f'}[\mathcal P'_{\mathsf{post}}]:
\Phi
\land
\equiv_{
\left(
\operatorname{src}_{D_f}(\mathcal V_{\mathsf{pre}}),
\operatorname{src}_{D'_{f'}}(\mathcal V'_{\mathsf{pre}})
\right)
}
\Longrightarrow
\equiv_{
\left(
\operatorname{tgt}_{D_f}(\mathcal V_{\mathsf{post}}),
\operatorname{tgt}_{D'_{f'}}(\mathcal V'_{\mathsf{post}})
\right)
}.
\end{aligned}
}
\]
The two static checks are read relative to the descriptor formulas in the
displayed precondition \(\Phi\). The \(\mathcal U\Rightarrow\mathcal W\) is the register input/output used
by the alignment.



\paragraph{Typical register schema alignments.}

For matching basis readout:
\[
\Gamma
\vdash
\mathsf{Read}_{b}^{E}(x;\bar q)
\cong
\mathsf{Read}_{b'}^{E'}(x';\bar q')
:
((b,\bar q),(b',\bar q'))
\Rightarrow
((b,x),(b',x'))
\]
when the descriptor formulas in the displayed Sift precondition entail
\[
E=E'.
\]

For split-vs-unsplit basis readout:
\[
\Gamma
\vdash
\mathsf{Read}_{b_0}^{m_0}(x_0;\bar q_0);
\mathsf{Read}_{b_1}^{m_1}(x_1;\bar q_1)
\cong
\mathsf{Read}_{b'}^{E}(x';\bar q')
:
\bigl(((b_0,\bar q_0),(b_1,\bar q_1)),(b',\bar q')^{f'}\bigr)
\Rightarrow
\bigl(((b_0,x_0),(b_1,x_1)),(b',x')^{f'}\bigr).
\]
The symmetric direction is also certified.

For matching computational-basis bit preparation:
\[
\Gamma
\vdash
\mathsf{PrepBits}^{E}(a;\bar q)
\cong
\mathsf{PrepBits}^{E'}(a';\bar q')
:
(a,a')
\Rightarrow
((a,\bar q),(a',\bar q'))
\]
when the descriptor formulas in the displayed Sift precondition entail
\[
E=E'.
\]

For split-vs-unsplit computational-basis bit preparation:
\[
\Gamma
\vdash
\mathsf{PrepBits}^{E}(a;\bar q)
\cong
\mathsf{PrepBits}^{m_0}(a'_0;\bar q'_0);
\mathsf{PrepBits}^{m_1}(a'_1;\bar q'_1)
:
\bigl(a,(a'_0,a'_1)^{\uparrow f'}\bigr)
\Rightarrow
\bigl((a,\bar q),((a'_0,\bar q'_0),(a'_1,\bar q'_1))^{\uparrow f'}\bigr).
\]
The symmetric direction is also certified.

For matching basis-indexed bit preparation:
\[
\Gamma
\vdash
\mathsf{PrepBits}^{E}_{b}(a;\bar q)
\cong
\mathsf{PrepBits}^{E'}_{b'}(a';\bar q')
:
((a,b),(a',b'))
\Rightarrow
((a,b,\bar q),(a',b',\bar q'))
\]
when the descriptor formulas in the displayed Sift precondition entail
\[
E=E'.
\]

For split-vs-unsplit basis-indexed bit preparation:
\[
\Gamma
\vdash
\mathsf{PrepBits}^{E}_{b}(a;\bar q)
\cong
\mathsf{PrepBits}^{m_0}_{b'_0}(a'_0;\bar q'_0);
\mathsf{PrepBits}^{m_1}_{b'_1}(a'_1;\bar q'_1)
:
\bigl((a,b),((a'_0,b'_0),(a'_1,b'_1))^{\uparrow f'}\bigr)
\Rightarrow
\bigl(
(a,b,\bar q),
((a'_0,b'_0,\bar q'_0),(a'_1,b'_1,\bar q'_1))^{\uparrow f'}
\bigr).
\]
The symmetric direction is also certified.

\paragraph{Derived sift-measure instance.}

Let \(m_c,m_k\) be the displayed lengths of the two selected target views.

Taking
\[
D_f[\mathcal P_{\mathsf{pre}}]
=
\mathbf{select}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\ \mathbf{for}\ b,\bar q,
\qquad
D'_{f'}[\mathcal P'_{\mathsf{post}}]
=
\mathbf{select}_{f'}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\ \mathbf{for}\ b',x',
\]
\[
\mathcal V_{\mathsf{pre}}=(b,\bar q),
\qquad
\mathcal V_{\mathsf{post}}=(b,x),
\]
gives:
\[
\begin{aligned}
\Gamma
\vdash\;&
(b_c,\bar q_c),(b_k,\bar q_k)
:=
\mathbf{select}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\ \mathbf{for}\ b,\bar q;
\\
&
\mathsf{Read}_{b_c}^{m_c}(x_c;\bar q_c);
\mathsf{Read}_{b_k}^{m_k}(x_k;\bar q_k)
\\
&\sim
\mathsf{Read}_{b'}^{J}(x';\bar q');
\\
&
(b'_c,x'_c),(b'_k,x'_k)
:=
\mathbf{select}_{f'}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\ \mathbf{for}\ b',x'
\\
&:
\equiv_{(f,f')}
\land
\equiv_{(b,b')}
\land
\equiv_{(\bar q,\bar q')}
\\
&\Longrightarrow
\equiv_{\bigl(
(b_c,x_c,b_k,x_k),
(b'_c,x'_c,b'_k,x'_k)
\bigr)} .
\end{aligned}
\]


\paragraph{Derived sift-prepare instance.}

Let \(m_c,m_k\) be the displayed lengths of the two selected source views.

For computational-basis preparation, taking
\[
D_f[\mathcal P_{\mathsf{pre}}]
=
\mathbf{merge}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\
\mathbf{for}\ (a_c,\bar q_c),(a_k,\bar q_k),
\]
\[
D'_{f'}[\mathcal P'_{\mathsf{post}}]
=
\mathbf{merge}_{f'}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\
\mathbf{for}\ (a'_c,\bar q'_c),(a'_k,\bar q'_k),
\]
\[
\mathcal V_{\mathsf{pre}}=a,
\qquad
\mathcal V_{\mathsf{post}}=(a,\bar q),
\]
gives:
\[
\begin{aligned}
\Gamma
\vdash\;&
(a,\bar q)
:=
\mathbf{merge}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\
\mathbf{for}\ (a_c,\bar q_c),(a_k,\bar q_k);
\\
&
\mathsf{PrepBits}^{J}(a;\bar q)
\\
&\sim
\mathsf{PrepBits}^{m_c}(a'_c;\bar q'_c);
\mathsf{PrepBits}^{m_k}(a'_k;\bar q'_k);
\\
&
(a',\bar q')
:=
\mathbf{merge}_{f'}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\
\mathbf{for}\ (a'_c,\bar q'_c),(a'_k,\bar q'_k)
\\
&:
\equiv_{(f,f')}
\land
\equiv_{(a_c,a'_c)}
\land
\equiv_{(a_k,a'_k)}
\\
&\Longrightarrow
\equiv_{(a,a')}
\land
\equiv_{(\bar q,\bar q')} .
\end{aligned}
\]

For basis-indexed preparation, taking
\[
D_f[\mathcal P_{\mathsf{pre}}]
=
\mathbf{merge}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\
\mathbf{for}\
(a_c,b_c,\bar q_c),(a_k,b_k,\bar q_k),
\]
\[
D'_{f'}[\mathcal P'_{\mathsf{post}}]
=
\mathbf{merge}_{f'}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\
\mathbf{for}\
(a'_c,b'_c,\bar q'_c),(a'_k,b'_k,\bar q'_k),
\]
\[
\mathcal V_{\mathsf{pre}}=(a,b),
\qquad
\mathcal V_{\mathsf{post}}=(a,b,\bar q),
\]
gives:
\[
\begin{aligned}
\Gamma
\vdash\;&
(a,b,\bar q)
:=
\mathbf{merge}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\
\mathbf{for}\ (a_c,b_c,\bar q_c),(a_k,b_k,\bar q_k);
\\
&
\mathsf{PrepBits}^{J}_{b}(a;\bar q)
\\
&\sim
\mathsf{PrepBits}^{m_c}_{b'_c}(a'_c;\bar q'_c);
\mathsf{PrepBits}^{m_k}_{b'_k}(a'_k;\bar q'_k);
\\
&
(a',b',\bar q')
:=
\mathbf{merge}_{f'}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\
\mathbf{for}\ (a'_c,b'_c,\bar q'_c),(a'_k,b'_k,\bar q'_k)
\\
&:
\equiv_{(f,f')}
\land
\equiv_{((a_c,b_c),(a'_c,b'_c))}
\land
\equiv_{((a_k,b_k),(a'_k,b'_k))}
\\
&\Longrightarrow
\equiv_{(a,a')}
\land
\equiv_{(b,b')}
\land
\equiv_{(\bar q,\bar q')} .
\end{aligned}
\]


\section{Syntax Sugar}
\label{app:syntax-sugar}

\begin{itemize}

    \item \textbf{Initialization of quantum variables:}
    \[
    \bar q[i]:=|1\rangle\stackrel{\triangle}{=}
    \bar q[i]:=|0\rangle;\ \bar q[i]\asteq X;
    \]
    
    \[
    \overline{q} := \ket{0}^{\otimes n}
    \stackrel{\triangle}{=}
    \bar{q}[1] := \ket{0};\ \cdots;\ \bar{q}[n] := \ket{0};\]

    \[
    \overline{q} := \ket{1}^{\otimes n}
    \stackrel{\triangle}{=}
    \bar{q}[1] := \ket{1};\ \cdots;\ \bar{q}[n] := \ket{1}.\]

    \item {\textbf{Dummy channel-order syntax sugar.}}
    
    {Private auxiliary channel-side systems must already belong
    to the fixed channel/adversarial workspace used with}
    \[
    {
    U_{\textbf{channel}}.
    }
    \]
    {They are ordinary systems outside the retained terminal QKD
    observation.}
    
    \item \textbf{Measurement in the computational basis:}
    For a qubit register
    \(\bar q=(\bar q[1],\ldots,\bar q[n])\)
    and a bit-valued classical register
    \(x=(x[1],\ldots,x[n])\), we write
    \[
    x[1,\ldots,n]
    :=
    \mathcal M_{\mathrm{com}}[\bar q[1,\ldots,n]]\]
    as syntactic sugar for
    \(x[1]:=\mathcal M_{\mathrm{com}}[\bar q[1]];
    \ \cdots;\
    x[n]:=\mathcal M_{\mathrm{com}}[\bar q[n]],\)
    where the single-qubit computational-basis measurement is
    \(\mathcal M_{\mathrm{com}}
    \stackrel{\triangle}{=}
    \{\ket 0\bra 0,\ket 1\bra 1\}.\)

    \item \(\mathsf{Read}_{b}^{E}(x;\bar q)\):
    For a bit-valued basis view \(b\), a bit-valued output view \(x\), and a
    quantum view \(\bar q\), define
    \[
    \mathsf{Read}_{b}^{E}(x;\bar q)
    \]
    as syntax sugar for
    \[
    \mathbf{for}^{E}\ i=1\ \mathbf{to}\ E
    \quad
    \mathbf{if}\ b[i]=0
    \rightarrow
    x[i]:=\mathcal M_{\mathrm{com}}[\bar q[i]],
    \]
    \[
    \hspace{27mm}
    \mathbf{else}
    \rightarrow
    x[i]:=\mathcal M_{\{+,-\}}[\bar q[i]]
    \quad
    \mathbf{end}.
    \]
    It is a descriptor-preserving register operation.

    \item \(\mathsf{PrepBits}^{E}(a;\bar q)\) and
    \(\mathsf{PrepBits}^{E}_{b}(a;\bar q)\):

    For a bit-valued input view \(a\), a bit-valued basis view \(b\), and a
    quantum view \(\bar q\), define basis-indexed preparation
    \[
    \mathsf{PrepBits}^{E}_{b}(a;\bar q)
    \]
    as syntax sugar for
    \[
    \mathbf{for}^{E}\ i=1\ \mathbf{to}\ E
    \quad
    \mathbf{if}\ b[i]=0
    \rightarrow S_0(i),
    \quad
    \mathbf{else}
    \rightarrow S_1(i)
    \quad
    \mathbf{end},
    \]
    where
    \[
    S_0(i)
    \stackrel{\triangle}{=}
    \mathbf{if}\ a[i]=0
    \rightarrow
    \bar q[i]:=\ket0,
    \quad
    \mathbf{else}
    \rightarrow
    \bar q[i]:=\ket1,
    \]
    and
    \[
    S_1(i)
    \stackrel{\triangle}{=}
    \mathbf{if}\ a[i]=0
    \rightarrow
    \bar q[i]:=\ket+,
    \quad
    \mathbf{else}
    \rightarrow
    \bar q[i]:=\ket- .
    \]

    Omitting the basis subscript means computational-basis preparation:
    \[
    \mathsf{PrepBits}^{E}(a;\bar q)
    \stackrel{\triangle}{=}
    \mathsf{PrepBits}^{E}_{\mathbf 0_E}(a;\bar q),
    \]
    where
    \[
    \mathbf 0_E[i]=0
    \qquad
    (1\le i\le E).
    \]

    Thus
    \[
    \mathsf{PrepBits}^{E}(a;\bar q)
    \]
    expands to
    \[
    \mathbf{for}^{E}\ i=1\ \mathbf{to}\ E
    \quad
    \mathbf{if}\ a[i]=0
    \rightarrow
    \bar q[i]:=\ket0,
    \quad
    \mathbf{else}
    \rightarrow
    \bar q[i]:=\ket1
    \quad
    \mathbf{end}.
    \]

    Both forms are descriptor-preserving register operations. Their output
    quantum state is determined by the displayed classical controls and not by
    the previous state of \(\bar q[i]\).

    \item \textbf{Classically indexed unitary operations on a fixed register:}
    For a unitary operator \(U\) acting on \(k\) qubits, we write
    \(\bar q[i_1,\ldots,i_k]\asteq U\)
    for applying \(U\) to ordered variables
    \(\bar q[i_1],\ldots,\bar q[i_k]\); \(k=1\) is primitive.
    Let \(U\stackrel{\triangle}{=}(U_i)_{1\le i\le K}\) be a finite family
    of unitary operators on the Hilbert space associated with \(\bar q\),
    with \(K\ge 1\), and let \(e\) be an \(\mathsf{Int}\)-typed expression.
    We write
    \[
    \bar q\asteq U(e)
    \]
    for the finite case expansion
    \[
    \textbf{if } e<1\lor e>K \rightarrow \textbf{abort},
    \ \textbf{else}\rightarrow S_1;\cdots;S_K,
    \]
    where, for each \(1\le i\le K\),
    \[
    S_i
    \stackrel{\triangle}{=}
    \textbf{if } e=i \rightarrow \bar q\asteq U_i,
    \ \textbf{else}\rightarrow\mathbf{skip}.
    \]
    Since \(S_i\) does not change \(e\), exactly one valid branch applies
    \(U_i\); out-of-range aborts.

    \item \textbf{Unitary operations on selected qubits:}
    Let \(1\le k\le n\), and let \(e,e_1,\ldots,e_k\) be
    \(\mathsf{Int}\)-typed expressions. The statement
    \[
    \bar q[e_1,\ldots,e_k]\asteq U(e),
    \]
    where \(U=(U_i)_{1\le i\le K}\) is as in the previous clause and each
    \(U_i\) acts on \(k\) qubits, applies \(U_i\) on the quantum systems
    \(\bar q[i_1],\ldots,\bar q[i_k]\) whenever \(e\) evaluates to \(i\)
    and each \(e_j\) evaluates to a distinct valid \(i_j\). The guard
    \[
    \exists\,1\le r\le k.\,(e_r<1\lor e_r>n)
    \ \lor\
    \exists\,1\le r<s\le k.\,(e_r=e_s)
    \]
    abbreviates the corresponding finite predicate. The statement denotes
    \[
    \textbf{if } B_{\mathrm{bad}}\rightarrow \textbf{abort},
    \ \textbf{else}\rightarrow S_1;S_2;\cdots;S_{|R|},
    \]
    where
    \(B_{\mathrm{bad}}
    \stackrel{\triangle}{=}
    \bigvee_{r=1}^{k}(e_r<1\lor e_r>n)
    \ \lor\
    \bigvee_{1\le r<s\le k}(e_r=e_s),\)
    and
    \(R
    \stackrel{\triangle}{=}
    \{(i_1,\ldots,i_k):
    1\le i_j\le n\ \text{ for all }j,\ \text{and }i_1,\ldots,i_k
    \text{ are distinct}\}.\)
    Fix an enumeration
    \[
    R=\{(i_1^\ell,\ldots,i_k^\ell):1\le \ell\le |R|\}.
    \]
    For each \(1\le \ell\le |R|\), define
    \[
    S_\ell
    \stackrel{\triangle}{=}
    \textbf{if }e_1=i_1^\ell\land\cdots\land e_k=i_k^\ell
    \rightarrow
    \bar q[i_1^\ell,\ldots,i_k^\ell]\asteq U(e),
    \ \textbf{else}\rightarrow\mathbf{skip}.
    \]

    \item \textbf{Preparation and measurement in the \(\{+,-\}\) basis:}
    For one qubit:
    \begin{align*}
        \bar q[i] := \ket{+}
        &\stackrel{\triangle}{=}
        \bar q[i] := \ket{0};\ \bar q[i]\asteq H,\\
        \bar q[i] := \ket{-}
        &\stackrel{\triangle}{=}
        \bar q[i] := \ket{0};\ \bar q[i]\asteq X;\ \bar q[i]\asteq H,\\
        c[t] := \mathcal M_{\{+,-\}}[\bar q[i]]
        &\stackrel{\triangle}{=}
        \bar q[i]\asteq H;\ c[t]:=\mathcal M_{\mathrm{com}}[\bar q[i]].
    \end{align*}

    \item \textbf{Boolean XOR notation:}
    For bit-valued expressions \(E_1,E_2\), we may use
    \[
    E_1\oplus E_2=0
    \quad\stackrel{\triangle}{=}\quad
    E_1=E_2,
    \qquad\text{and}\qquad
    E_1\oplus E_2=1
    \quad\stackrel{\triangle}{=}\quad
    E_1\neq E_2.
    \]
    Assignment notation
    \[
    x[t] := E_1\oplus E_2
    \]
    as syntactic sugar for
    \[
    \textbf{if } E_1=E_2 \rightarrow x[t]:=0,
    \ \textbf{else}\rightarrow x[t]:=1.
    \]


    \item \textbf{CNOT gate:}
    For \(k\ge 1\), we write
    \(\bar q[e_1,\ldots,e_k,e_{k+1},\ldots,e_{2k}]\asteq \mathrm{CNOT}\)
    for the parallel application of \(k\) CNOT gates, where \(\bar q[e_j]\)
    is the control and \(\bar q[e_{k+j}]\) is the target of the \(j\)-th CNOT
    gate:
    \[
    \bar q[e_1,\ldots,e_k,e_{k+1},\ldots,e_{2k}]\asteq \mathrm{CNOT}
    \stackrel{\triangle}{=}
    \bar q[e_1,e_{k+1},e_2,e_{k+2},\ldots,e_k,e_{2k}]
    \asteq \mathrm{CNOT}^{\otimes k}.
    \]
    Range and distinctness come from selected-qubit unitary sugar. If
    \(\bar q=(\bar q[1],\bar q[2])\) is a two-qubit register, then
    \(\bar q\asteq \mathrm{CNOT}
    \quad\text{stands for}\quad
    \bar q[1,2]\asteq \mathrm{CNOT},\)
    with \(\bar q[1]\) as control and \(\bar q[2]\) as target.

    \item \textbf{Finite for-loop notation.}

    For any fixed protocol length \(M\) and any statement schema \(S(i)\), we
    write
    \[
    \mathbf{for}^{M}\ i=1\ \mathbf{to}\ M
    \quad S(i)
    \quad \mathbf{end}
    \]
    as the finite expansion
    \[
    S(1);S(2);\cdots;S(M).
    \]
    This is fixed finite sequencing; it is not a while-loop.

\item \(\mathbf{select}_{f}\):

Let \(g\) be an indexed logical descriptor view, and let \(g_0,g_1\) be
logical lists with
\[
\operatorname{sort}(g_0)=\operatorname{sort}(g_1)=\operatorname{sort}(g).
\]
Let \(f\) be a bit-valued filter descriptor. The command
\[
(g_0,g_1)
:=
\mathbf{select}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\ \mathbf{for}\ g
\]
is well formed only when \(J\) is the whole current length of \(g\):
\[
J=\mathbf{length}(g)
\]
or \(J=N\) with
\[
N=\mathbf{length}(g).
\]

It defines \(g_0\) and \(g_1\) as the \(f=0\) and \(f=1\) subviews of \(g\),
preserving relative order in each fiber.

The package notation
\[
(\mathcal P_0,\mathcal P_1)
:=
\mathbf{select}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\ \mathbf{for}\ \mathcal P
\]
is componentwise.

\(\mathbf{select}_{f}\) constructs descriptor views, not value/state copies.

\item \(\mathbf{merge}_{f}\):

Let \(g\) be a target descriptor view, let \(g_0,g_1\) be source views, and let
\(f\) be a bit-valued filter descriptor. The command
\[
g
:=
\mathbf{merge}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\ \mathbf{for}\ g_0,g_1
\]
is well formed only when \(J\) is the whole merged length:
\[
J=\mathbf{length}(g_0)+\mathbf{length}(g_1)
\]
or \(J=N\) with
\[
N=\mathbf{length}(g_0)+\mathbf{length}(g_1).
\]

It interleaves \(g_0,g_1\) according to \(f\), preserving source order.

The package notation
\[
\mathcal P
:=
\mathbf{merge}_{f}^{N}\ \mathbf{from}\ J\ \mathbf{for}\ \mathcal P_0,\mathcal P_1
\]
is componentwise.

\(\mathbf{merge}_{f}\) constructs descriptor views, not value/state copies.
    
    \item \textbf{CSS-QEC syntax sugar.}

    The abbreviation
    \[
    \bar u:=QEC(\bar r)
    \]
    abbreviates CSS correction sugar:
    syndrome measurement, decoder lookups, indexed Pauli corrections, and CSS
    decoding.


    \item \textbf{Fixed finite classical-map syntax sugars.}

    Let
    \[
    F:D_1\times\cdots\times D_s\to D
    \]
    be a fixed external classical map over finite protocol domains. The command
    \[
    y:=F(x_1,\ldots,x_s)
    \]
    is finite case analysis over \(D_1\times\cdots\times D_s\), using only
    conditionals and constant assignments. For each tuple
    \[
    d=(d_1,\ldots,d_s)\in D_1\times\cdots\times D_s,
    \]
    let
    \[
    c_d=F(d_1,\ldots,d_s).
    \]
    Then \(y:=F(x_1,\ldots,x_s)\) expands into the finite sequence of guarded
    assignments
    \[
    \prod_{d\in D_1\times\cdots\times D_s}
    \left(
    \mathbf{if}\ x_1=d_1\land\cdots\land x_s=d_s
    \rightarrow y:=c_d,
    \ \mathbf{else}\rightarrow\mathbf{skip}
    \right),
    \]
    for any fixed enumeration of the finite domain.

    Vector-valued fixed maps are expanded componentwise. Thus commands such as
    \[
    k_b:=\mathsf{qecBob}(k',x-\nu_k),
    \qquad
    k_a:=\mathsf{qecAlice}(k,x-\nu_k),
    \qquad
    \hat e_X:=D_X(s_Z),
    \qquad
    \hat e_Z:=D_Z(s_X)
    \]
    are finite classical-map syntax sugars, not primitives.

    \item \textbf{Pauli-parity and CSS-syndrome measurement.}
    
    Matrices here are fixed external data, not sampled program variables.
    
    Let \(h=(h_1,\ldots,h_N)\in\{0,1\}^{N}\) be a fixed binary protocol vector.
    Define
    \[
    \operatorname{supp}(h)
    \stackrel{\triangle}{=}
    \{t: h_t=1\}.
    \]
    For a quantum block
    \[
    \bar r=(\bar r[1],\ldots,\bar r[N]),
    \]
    define
    \[
    Z(h)\stackrel{\triangle}{=}\bigotimes_{t=1}^{N}Z_t^{h_t},
    \qquad
    X(h)\stackrel{\triangle}{=}\bigotimes_{t=1}^{N}X_t^{h_t}.
    \]
    The syndrome bit convention is
    \[
    0\equiv +1\text{ eigenvalue},
    \qquad
    1\equiv -1\text{ eigenvalue}.
    \]
    
    For logical quantum views \(u,v\), write
    \[
    \operatorname{CNOT}_{u\rightarrow v}
    \]
    for the selected-qubit CNOT update with ordinary liveness, disjointness,
    and dimension obligations.
    
    If
    \[
    \operatorname{supp}(h)=\{t_1<\cdots<t_w\},
    \]
    then the \(Z(h)\)-parity measurement
    \[
    s:=\mathsf{MeasZCheck}_{h}(\bar r;a)
    \]
    is syntactic sugar for
    \[
    a:=\ket0;
    \quad
    \operatorname{CNOT}_{\bar r[t_1]\rightarrow a};
    \quad\cdots\quad;
    \operatorname{CNOT}_{\bar r[t_w]\rightarrow a};
    \quad
    s:=\mathcal M_{\mathrm{com}}[a].
    \]
    If \(w=0\), the CNOT sequence is empty and the measurement deterministically
    returns \(s=0\).
    
    The \(X(h)\)-parity measurement
    \[
    s:=\mathsf{MeasXCheck}_{h}(\bar r;a)
    \]
    is syntactic sugar for
    \[
    a:=\ket0;
    \quad
    a\asteq H;
    \quad
    \operatorname{CNOT}_{a\rightarrow \bar r[t_1]};
    \quad\cdots\quad;
    \operatorname{CNOT}_{a\rightarrow \bar r[t_w]};
    \quad
    a\asteq H;
    \quad
    s:=\mathcal M_{\mathrm{com}}[a].
    \]
    If \(w=0\), the CNOT sequence is empty and the measurement deterministically
    returns \(s=0\).
    
    These expand to initialization, Hadamard, CNOT, sequencing, and binary
    measurement before denotation.
    
    Let
    \[
    H_Z\in\{0,1\}^{r_Z\times N},
    \qquad
    H_X\in\{0,1\}^{r_X\times N}
    \]
    be fixed external CSS parity-check matrices satisfying
    \[
    H_XH_Z^{\mathsf T}=0
    \quad\text{over }\mathbb F_2.
    \]
    Write \(h^Z_u\) for the \(u\)-th row of \(H_Z\), and \(h^X_v\) for the
    \(v\)-th row of \(H_X\).
    
    For syndrome output registers
    \[
    s_Z[1,\ldots,r_Z],
    \qquad
    s_X[1,\ldots,r_X],
    \]
    and ancilla blocks
    \[
    a_Z[1,\ldots,r_Z],
    \qquad
    a_X[1,\ldots,r_X],
    \]
    define
    \[
    (s_Z,s_X):=
    \mathsf{CSSSyn}_{H_Z,H_X}(\bar r;a_Z,a_X)
    \]
    as syntactic sugar for
    \[
    \mathbf{for}^{r_Z}\ u=1\ \mathbf{to}\ r_Z
    \quad
    s_Z[u]:=\mathsf{MeasZCheck}_{h^Z_u}(\bar r;a_Z[u])
    \quad
    \mathbf{end};
    \]
    \[
